Calculating Debt Division After Loss of Pledged Slave's Eye
Detailed arithmetic for debt division in rahn injury

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi arithmetic method to calculate proportional debt reduction when a pledged slave is injured.

Core Idea
When a pledged slave is injured, debt and value are reduced proportionally based on each party's initial share.

This passage presents a specific Hanafi calculation for a damage scenario in rahn. Two parties have claims on a pledged slave: the 'amputated' (maqtua) is owed debt, and the 'cutter' (qatia) caused the injury. When the slave loses an eye, its value halves. The method shows how each party's debt is proportionally forgiven, illustrating the precision of Hanafi fiqh in financial transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify parties and initial shares
Recognize that the maqtua (creditor) and her child have shares 40 and 5 from a base of 45. The qatia (debtor) and her child have a separate share of 20 divided into 5 parts.
The numbers come from the original debt relationships.
2
Compute transfer from maqtua to qatia
Half of maqtua's 40 (i.e., 20) is transferred to qatia. Now qatia holds 20 in the slave's value.
This transfer reflects partial repayment or compensation.
3
Divide qatia's share between qatia and her child
Qatia's 20 is divided into 5 shares: 4 for her child, 16 for herself. This ratio is maintained from the original 9:5 split.
The child's share is 1/5 of qatia's total.
4
Apply injury: halve the slave's value
Losing an eye reduces the slave's value by half. Therefore, each party's claim is halved: maqtua's claim drops from 20 to 10, qatia's from 16 to 8.
The reduction is proportional to the loss in value.
5
Calculate remaining debt and redemption
Total original debt was 45 (maqtua 40 + child 5). After reduction, remaining debt = 18 (10+5+? Actually careful: maqtua's remaining 10, child's 5, qatia's remaining 8? No, qatia is debtor. The text says remaining debt is 18, remaining slave value is 27, so redemption fraction is 18/27 = 2/3? But text says three-fifths. This discrepancy indicates the need to re-read; the calculation likely yields 18/30? However, the key point is the method.
The final fraction may be 3/5 if the base is 45 and remaining value 30? Re-examine.

Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi ruling on how to calculate the reduction of debt when a pledged slave (called 'the amputated') is injured, specifically losing an eye. The author gives a step-by-step arithmetic method. First, the base number (asl al-mas'alah) is determined from the shares of the amputated and her child (9 and 5) giving 45. The amputated's 40 shares are halved to give 20 to the cutter (the one who caused the injury). Then the cutter's share of 20 is divided among herself and her child in a ratio yielding 4 and 16 respectively (since 20 ÷ 5 = 4 per share). When the slave loses an eye, half the value is lost, so half from each party's shares is deducted: from the amputated's original 20, 10 falls; from the cutter's 16, 8 falls. The remaining debt is 18 and remaining value 27, so the slave is redeemed with 18/27 = 2/3? However the text says three-fifths, which may refer to 18/30? The exact interpretation requires careful reading, but the method shows proportional reduction specific to the Hanafi school.

Dividing Debts in Cases of Multiple Pledged Slaves Killing Each Other with Offspring
Detailed case analysis of debt division in a complex chain of killings among pledged slaves.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi method of dividing a debt among multiple pledged slaves when killings and births occur, and calculate the shares using proportional division with recalibration.

Core Idea
Debt among pledged slaves is divided proportionally; killings create substitutions that require careful recalculation.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq presents a complex scenario involving a series of killings among pledged slaves and their offspring. The Hanafi jurists have devised a rigorous method for dividing the debt among the surviving parties, ensuring fair distribution. In this lesson, we will walk through the calculation step by step, understanding how values are converted into shares and how the division is adjusted when errors are discovered.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and their values
List all slaves involved (pledged slaves, their offspring) and their respective values in dirhams. Convert values into shares based on a unit (e.g., every 100 dirhams = one share).
The values are given in the text: first mother 1000, her son 1000, etc.
2
Determine the sequence of events
Note the chronology of killings and births: first mother kills a 100-dirham slave, then that slave kills a 1000-dirham slave, etc. Each killer takes the place of the killed party.
The chain is: Mother (M1) kills J1 (value 100), J1 (now paid) gives birth to S1 (value 1000), then J1 kills J2 (value 1000), etc.
3
Apply the initial division
Divide the debt among the first set of parties based on equal values. For example, the first killed and her son are split in halves, and further splits are done using shares.
The initial division yields 22 shares total.
4
Handle substitutions and recalibrate
When a killer takes the place of multiple killed parties, her value and her offspring's value replace the previous shares. This may cause an imbalance requiring recalculation (istinaf al-qisma).
The second killer (the 1000-dirham slave) replaces the first killer and her two sons, leading to 21 shares.
5
Final division after correction
After the second killer dies, her share is divided between her son and the surviving parties. The final division results in 31 shares, with specific shares for each son.
The text concludes: one son gets 10 shares, the other son gets 10 shares from a further division, and the pledgor pays half of some shares.

Defect and Injury in Pledged Slaves: Intra-Hanafi Disputes
Rulings on defect and injury in pledged slaves, with intra-Hanafi disagreements

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rules on defects and injuries in pledged slaves and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Zufar on the pledgor's options.

Core Idea
A connected increase in a pledge does not reduce the debt, but the Sahibayn consider the initial defect value.

This lesson examines several scenarios involving defects and injuries to a pledged slave, highlighting the nuanced disagreements among the Hanafi masters. You will learn how the disappearance of a pre-existing defect, an injury by a third party, and the killing of the slave by another slave affect the pledged property and the debt. The positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani, and Zufar are presented, allowing you to see the legal reasoning behind each view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first case and the ruling
Start with the scenario of a female slave with a white spot in one eye pledged for 1000. Note that after the pledge, the sound eye is lost, reducing value to 200. The ruling: four-fifths of the debt is discharged.
The debt reduction is proportional to value loss.
2
Examine the effect of the white spot disappearing
If the white spot disappears spontaneously, Abu Hanifa rules no reduction because it is a connected increase (ziyada muttasila). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree, considering what the spot would have reduced at pledge time.
Understand the concept of ziyada muttasila vs munsalila.
3
Analyze the injury case and the arsh calculation
A third party strikes the eye, causing whitening. The compensation (arsh) is 800. The pledgor can redeem using the arsh, but only five-ninths of the debt. Then if the remaining sound eye is lost, further reduction occurs.
The arsh is the difference in value, and the redemption fraction is carefully computed.
4
Compare the views on slave killing the pledged slave
If a slave worth 100 kills the pledged slave and is handed over as compensation, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say the pledgor must pay the full debt to redeem. Muhammad gives a choice: pay all or hand over the killer slave. Zufar says the killer becomes a pledge for 100.
This is a pure intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. Note the reasoning: substitution vs change in subject.
5
Apply the post-pledgor death rules
If the pledgor dies, the executor sells the pledge and pays debts. If no executor, the judge appoints one. Pledging estate property by the executor to a creditor is invalid.
This is consistent with general agency and guardianship rules.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا كانت جارية بإحدى عينيها بياض مرهونة بألف وهي قيمتها فذهبت العين الأخرى وصارت تساوي مائتين ذهب من الدين أربعة أخماسه، فإن ذهب البياض عن العين الأولى لم يعد شيء من الدين لأنها زيادة متصلة حدثت بعد الرهن فلا تكون مضمونة فإن ضرب رجل هذه العين فصارت بيضاء غرم ثمانمائة ويفتك الراهن الجارية الأرش بخمسة اتساع الدين فإن عميت الجارية بعد ذلك بأن ذهبت العين التي كانت صحيحة بعد الرهن فالعمى يوجب نقصان ثمان مائة من قيمتها وقد ذهب عن أربعة أخماسها فذهب أربعة أخماس الدين ويبقى خمسة ويبقى أيضاً حصة الأرش أربعة أخماس الدين كذلك الباقي من الدين خمسة أسهم من تسعة فيفتك الرهن خمسة اتساع. رجل رهن جارية بأحد عينيها بياض قيمتها ألف بألف فذهب البياض وصارت قيمتها ألفين ثم ابيضت الصحيحة وعادت قيمتها إلى ألف فعند أبي يوسف ومحمد ينظر إلى ما كان ينقص هذا البياض، ولو كان البياض على حاله فإن نقص أربعة أخماس القيمة بطل أربعة أخماس الدين وبيان تعليل كل المسائل ينظر في المبسوط . قال رحمه الله : (فإن قتله عبد قيمته مائة فدفعه به افتكه بكل الدين) وهذا قول أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف. وقال محمد : هو بالخيار إن شاء افتكه بجميع الدين، وإن شاء دفع العبد المدفوع إلى المرتهن بدينه ولاشيء عليه غيره. وقال زفر يصير رهناً بمائة وسقط من الدين بقدر الغاية. قلنا إن العبد الثاني قام مقام الأول لحماً ودماً ولو كان الأول قائماً وانتقص السعر لا ينقص الدين وهي على الخلاف ولمحمد أن المرهون تغير في ضمان المرتهن فيخير الراهن كالبيع والمغصوب إذا كان قيمة كل واحد منهما ألف وقتل كل واحد منهما عبداً قيمته مائة أن كل واحد من المشتري والمغصوب منه بالخيار إن شاء أخذ القاتل ولا شيء له غيره، وإن شاء فسخ المشتري البيع ورجع المغصوب منه بقيمة العبد، ولهما أن التغيير لم يظهر في نفس العبد لقيام الثاني مقام الأول لحماً ودماً لا يجوز تمليكه من المرتهن بغير رضاه، وعلى هذا الخلاف لو تراجع سعره حتى صار يساوي مائة ثم قتل عبداً يساوي مائة فدفع به. قال رحمه الله : (وإن مات الراهن باع وصيه الرهن وقضى الدين لأن الوصي قائم مقام الموصي له أن يبيع الرهن فكذا الوصية. قال رحمه الله: (فإن لم يكن له وصى نصب القاضي له وصياً وأمر ببيعه) وفعل ذلك إلى القاضي لأن القاضي نصب ناظراً لحقوق المسلمين، إذا عجزوا عن النظر لأنفسهم وقد تعين النظر في نصيب الوصي ليؤدي ما عليه لغيره ويستوفي حقوقه من غيره، ولو كان على الميت دين فرهن الوصي بعض التركة عند غريم له من غرمائه لم يجز وكان
If a female slave with a white spot in one of her eyes is pledged for a thousand, and she is worth that, then the other eye goes and she becomes worth two hundred, four-fifths of the debt goes. If the white spot disappears from the first eye, nothing of the debt is restored, because it is a connected increase occurring after the pledge, so it is not guaranteed. If a man strikes that eye and it becomes white, he pays eight hundred, and the pledgor redeems the slave with the arsh (compensation) at five-ninths of the debt. Then if the slave becomes blind after that, in that the eye that was sound goes after the pledge, blindness causes a decrease of eight hundred in value, and it had gone from four-fifths of her, so four-fifths of the debt goes, and five remains, and also the share of the arsh is four-fifths of the debt, likewise the remaining of the debt is five shares out of nine, so the pledge is redeemed at five-ninths. A man pledged a female slave with a white spot in one eye, worth a thousand for a thousand, then the white spot goes and she becomes worth two thousand, then the sound eye becomes white and her value returns to a thousand. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, one looks at what this white spot would have decreased; and if the white spot were in its original state, if it decreased four-fifths of the value, four-fifths of the debt is voided. The explanation of the reasoning for all the cases is to be looked at in al-Mabsut. He (the author) said: 'If a slave worth one hundred kills him (the pledged slave) and he (the pledgor) pays him with that, he redeems it with all the debt.' This is the saying of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. And Muhammad said: He has the choice: if he wishes, he redeems it with all the debt, and if he wishes, he gives the paid slave to the mortgagee for his debt, and nothing else is upon him. And Zufar said: It becomes a pledge for one hundred, and from the debt the amount of the loss falls. We said: The second slave stands in the place of the first in flesh and blood, and if the first were standing and the price decreased, the debt does not decrease, and it is on the disagreement. For Muhammad, the mortgaged property changed in the mortgagee's guarantee, so the pledgor is given a choice like in sale and usurpation, if the value of each of them is a thousand and each of them kills a slave worth one hundred, each of the buyer and the one from whom it was usurped has the choice: if he wishes, he takes the killer and nothing else is for him, and if wishes, the buyer rescinds the sale and the one from whom it was taken returns to the value of the slave. For them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), the change did not appear in the slave itself because the second stood in the place of the first in flesh and blood, it is not permissible to transfer ownership to the mortgagee without his consent. On this disagreement, if its price returns until it becomes worth one hundred, then it kills a slave worth one hundred and pays with it. He (the author) said: 'If the pledgor dies, his executor sells the pledge and pays off the debt, because the executor stands in the place of the testator, he has the right to sell the pledge, and so the executorship.' He said: 'If he does not have an executor, the judge appoints an executor for him and orders its sale.' This is done by the judge because the judge is appointed as a supervisor for the rights of Muslims when they are unable to look out for themselves, and the supervision has been determined in the share of the executor to pay what is due from him to others and to receive his rights from others. If the deceased had a debt and the executor pledged some of the estate with one of his creditors, it is not permissible. And there was...
Source pages p. 512

Commentary
This passage addresses several issues concerning defects and injuries in pledged slaves, along with intra-Hanafi disagreements. First, the case of a pledged slave with a pre-existing white spot in one eye: if the sound eye is lost, the debt is reduced by four-fifths; if the white spot disappears spontaneously, no reduction occurs because it is a connected increase (ziyada muttasila) arising after the pledge. If a third party strikes the eye, the tortfeasor pays compensation (arsh), and the pledgor redeems the slave with that arsh at five-ninths of the debt. A further scenario involves the white spot disappearing and then the sound eye turning white: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider what the white spot would have reduced initially. Then, the passage presents a dispute regarding a slave that kills the pledged slave: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf rule that if the killer is given as compensation, the pledgor must pay the entire debt to redeem, while Muhammad gives the pledgor a choice to either pay all or surrender the killer slave. Zufar holds that the killer slave becomes a new pledge for the diminished value. The Hanafi response to Muhammad is that the substitute slave stands in the place of the original, so no change in the subject matter, thus no choice. Finally, rules on the death of the pledgor: the executor sells the pledge, and if no executor, the judge appoints one. The passage ends with a note that if the executor pledges estate property to a creditor, it is invalid.

Key Terms
بياض (bayāḍ): A white spot in the eye, a type of defect
أرش (arsh): Compensation paid by a tortfeasor for causing injury to a slave
الوصي (al-waṣī): The executor appointed to manage the estate of a deceased pledgor

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a white spot disappears from a pledged slave's eye after the pledge, what happens to the debt?
A) The debt is reduced by the value of the defect
B) The debt remains unchanged
C) The debt is cancelled entirely
D) The debtor must pay additional compensation

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi pledge law, a connected increase (ziyada muttasila) does not affect the debt, but the Sahibayn disagree regarding pre-existing defects.

Proportional Revival of a Pawned Item: The Tanned Hide Case
Commentary on the ruling of a dead pawned sheep's tanned hide and its legal status

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of proportional revival of a pawn when part of the pawned item is revived (e.g., tanning a hide) and distinguish it from the sale case.

Core Idea
A pawn revives proportionally if part of it is revived after destruction.

Imagine a sheep is pawned for a debt. The sheep dies, but its hide is tanned, giving it new value. Does the pawn contract survive? The Hanafi school addresses this classic case to clarify how a pawn can be partially revived. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proof, and a key dispute about tanning with valuable materials.

Guided Path
1
State the basic ruling
Identify the act: a pawned sheep dies, its hide is tanned. What is the hukm on the hide? It remains a pledge for its value at the time of tanning.
2
Analyze the dalil (qiyas)
The proof is qiyas: the pawn contract is 'obstructed' by destruction, not annulled. Reviving part of the subject matter brings back the ruling proportionally. Contrast with sale, where destruction annuls the contract fully.
The key difference is that sale is annulled before delivery, pawn is not.
3
Consider variations in value
If the sheep's value equals the debt, the hide is fully pawned. If the sheep's value exceeds the debt, the hide is partially pawned proportionally. If the sheep's value is less, the debt is reduced proportionally upon destruction.
The text gives a detailed calculation from al-Mabsut.
4
Examine the effect of tanning with valuable materials
If the mortgagee tans the hide with items of value (e.g., chemicals), a new right of retention arises for the added value. Does this annul the original pawn? Two opinions are presented.
The second opinion (that the original pawn remains) appears stronger based on the commentary.
5
Determine the operative ruling (mufta bihi)
Although the text does not explicitly choose, the detailed rebuttal of the first opinion and the reasoning that the description follows the essence suggest that the first pledge remains, and the mortgagee retains the hide for both the original debt and the added value until both are paid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ولو رهن شاة قيمتها عشرة بعشرة فماتت فدبغ جلدها وهو يساوي درهماً فهو رهن بدرهم لأن الرهن يتعذر بالهلاك وإذا أحيا بعض المحل يعود الحكم بقدره بخلاف ما إذا ماتت الشاة المبيعة قبل القبض فديغ جلدها حيث لا المرتهن بشيء لا قيمة له، وإن دبغه بشيء له قيمة كان للمرتهن حق حبسه بما زاد الدباغ فيه كما لو غصب جلد ميتة ودبغه بشيء له قيمة ثم قيل يبطل الرهن فيه حتى إذا أدى الراهن ما زاد الدباغ فيه أخذه وليس له أن يحبسه بالدين لأنه لما حبسه بالدين الثاني فصار به محبوساً حكماً خرج من أن يكون رهناً بالأول حكماً كما إذا رهنه حقيقة بأن رهن الرهن بدين آخر غير ما كان محبوساً به فإنه يخرج عن الأول ويكون رهناً بالثاني فكذا هذا. وقيل: لا يبطل لأن الشيء إنما يبطل بما هو فوقه أو مثله ولا يبطل بما هو دونه كالمبيع بألف إذا باعه ثانياً . بأقل أو بأكثر يبطل لأنه مثله ولا يبطل بالإجارة والرهن لأن الثاني دون الأول لأنه إنما يستحق حبس الجلد بالمائة التي اتصلت بالجلد بحكم الدباغ وتلك المالية تبع للجدل لأنها وصف له والوصف دائماً يتبع الأصل فالرهن الأول رهن بما هو أصل بنفسه وليس بتبع لغيره وهو الدين فيكون أقوى من الثاني فلم الذي كان بإزائه وهو درهم وسقط أربعة التي بإزاء اللحم

كتاب الرهن باب التصرف في الرهن والجناية عليه وجنايته على غيره
بدرهم وإنماء الرهن كالولد والتمر واللبن والصوف للراهن وهو رهن مع الأصل ويهلك مجاناً وإن هلك الأصل وبقي النماء فك بحصته ويقسم الدين على قيمته يوم لأنه لم يزل التوى عن اللحم وكان الباقي من الدين ستة فصار الجلد مرهوناً بستة مضموناً بدرهم لأن كل جزء من أجزاء الشاة مرهون بجميع الدين مضمون بمقدار قيمته فكذا الجلد. هذا إذا دبغ بشيء لا قيمة له، فإن دبغ بشيء له قيمة فإنه يستحق المرتهن الحبس بما زاد الدباغ فيه كالغصب، فإذا استحق الحبس بدين آخر حادث هل يبطل الرهن الأول؟ قال الفقيه أبو جعفر الهندواني رحمه الله تعالى : لقائل أن يقول يبطل الرهن الأول في حق الجلد ويصير الجلد رهناً بما زاد الدباغ فيه كما لو رهن الراهن هذه العين بدين حادث، ولقائل أن يقول يبقى الرهن الأول ويصير محبوساً بقيمة الدباغ حتى لا يكون للراهن أن يفتكه ما لم يرد ما بإزائه من الدين وقيمة الدباغ
Chapter of pledge, section on disposition over the pledge and injury upon it and its injury upon others. 515. And if someone pawns a sheep worth ten for ten, and it dies, then its hide is tanned and it is worth one dirham, it is a pledge for one dirham because the pledge is obstructed by destruction, and if part of the subject matter is revived, the rule returns proportionally. Unlike if a sold sheep dies before delivery and its hide is tanned, where the sale does not return proportionally because the sale is annulled by destruction before delivery. So for the pledge it is obstructed by destruction. Some shaykhs say the sale returns. His saying 'and it is worth one dirham' indicates that value at the time of tanning is considered, and similarly his saying 'it is a pledge for one dirham'. They said this is if the value of the hide at the time of pledge was one dirham. And if its value at the time of pledge was two dirhams, then the hide is a pledge for two dirhams, and that is known by valuation: the pawned sheep is appraised unskinned, then skinned, and the difference is the hide's value. This if the sheep was entirely secured; if part was a trust, meaning its value exceeded the debt, then the hide is partly a trust proportionally, so it is a pledge for its share of the debt. They said this is if the mortgagee tanned it with something of no value. But if he tanned it with something of value, the mortgagee has a right to retain it for what the tanning added, as when someone usurps the hide of a dead animal and tans it with something of value. Then it is said the pledge is annulled regarding it, so that when the pledgor pays what the tanning added, he takes it and cannot retain it for the debt, because when he retained it for the second debt, it became by that retained constructively, and it left being a pledge for the first constructively, as if he actually pawned it: if someone pawns a pledge for another debt other than what it was retained for, it leaves the first and becomes a pledge for the second. So likewise this. And it is said it is not annulled because a thing is only annulled by what is above it or equal, not by what is inferior, like a sale for a thousand if he sells it a second time for less or more, it is annulled because it is equal; but it is not annulled by lease or pledge because the second is inferior to the first. For he only deserves to retain the hide for the value that attached to the hide by virtue of tanning, and that wealth is a follower of the hide because it is a description of it, and the description always follows the original. So the first pledge is a pledge for what is an essence itself, not a follower of another, which is the debt, so it is stronger than the second, so the first is not lifted by the second. Al-Mabsut says: If its value exceeded the debt, as twenty and the debt ten, consider: if the hide is worth one dirham and the rest nineteen, the hide is a pledge for half a dirham. If its value is less than the debt, as it equals five, the hide one dirham, the meat four: four dirhams drop from the debt, and the hide remains a pledge for six, because by destruction five dirhams dropped from the debt—the amount of the value of the pledge—and the debt remains five. So if he delivers the hide, he has revived one fifth of the pledge, so one fifth of the debt that was its counterpart returns, which is one dirham, and the four that were in exchange for the meat dropped. From it. 516. Last and it is. Chapter of pledge, section on disposition over the pledge and injury upon it and its injury upon others. By a dirham and increase of the pledge like offspring, dates, milk, and wool belongs to the pledgor, and it is a pledge with the original, and it perishes for free. And if the original perishes and the increase remains, it is redeemed by its share, and the debt is divided over its value on the day, because the damage from the meat has not ceased. And what remained of the debt was six, so the hide became pawned for six, secured by one dirham, because every part of the sheep is pawned for the entire debt and secured by the measure of its value. So likewise the hide. This is if he tanned it with something of no value. If he tanned it with something of value, then the mortgagee deserves retention for what the tanning added, as in usurpation. So when he deserves retention for another new debt, does the first pledge become void? Al-Faqih Abu Ja'far al-Hindwani, may Allah have mercy on him, said: One may say the first pledge becomes void regarding the hide, and the hide becomes a pledge for what the tanning added, as if the pledgor pawned this item for a new debt. And one may say the first pledge remains, and it becomes retained by the value of the tanning, so that the pledgor cannot redeem it until he pays both its counterpart of debt and the value of the tanning.
Source pages p. 515

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on a ruling from the matn about a pawned sheep that dies. The core rule: if a pawned item perishes and a part of it is revived (like tanning the hide), the pawn obligation revives proportionally. The commentator first states the ruling: a sheep pawned for ten dirhams dies, its hide is tanned and worth one dirham—the hide remains a pledge for one dirham. He supports this by analogy: just as reviving part of the subject matter brings back the rule proportionally, the pawn revives in that part. He contrasts this with a sale, where if a sold animal dies before delivery, the sale is fully annulled and does not revive even if the hide is tanned. Some shaykhs hold that the sale also returns, but the preferred view in pawn is that it returns. The commentator clarifies that the value considered is that at the time of tanning, not at the time of the pawn agreement. He then discusses cases where the sheep's value exceeds the debt (part is trust/amanah), so the hide is only partially pawned. A major part of the discussion concerns when the mortgagee tans the hide using materials of value. This creates a second right of retention (habs) for the added value. Does this second right annul the original pawn? Two opinions are cited: one says it annuls, likening it to pawning a pawn for a new debt; the other says it does not annul because the original pawn right pertains to the essence of the hide, while the tanning value is a description that follows the essence. The passage also includes a quotation from al-Mabsut explaining the calculation when the sheep's value is less or more than the debt, and how the debt is reduced proportionally upon destruction of the meat. Finally, it presents the opinion of al-Hindwani confirming the two perspectives on the effect of tanning with valuable material.

Key Terms
الرهن (ar-rahn): A contract of pledge where an asset is held as security for a debt. If the asset perishes, the debt is discharged up to its value.
الدباغ (ad-dibagh): The process of tanning a hide, which makes it valuable and usable. It is a form of reviving the subject matter.
الحبس (al-habs): The right of retention: the mortgagee's right to keep the pawned item until the debt is paid. Here it also refers to the right to retain the hide for the added value of tanning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man pawns a sheep worth 10 dirhams for a debt of 10 dirhams. The sheep dies, and its hide is tanned. After tanning, the hide is worth 2 dirhams. What is the status of the hide as a pawn?
A) The hide is not a pawn because the sheep was destroyed.
B) The hide is a pawn for 1 dirham because that was the value at the time of the original pawn.
C) The hide is a pawn for 2 dirhams because that is its current value at tanning.
D) The hide is a pawn for 10 dirhams because the original debt remains intact.

Key Takeaway
A pawn revives proportionally if part of the pawned item is revived after destruction; the revived portion remains pledged for its share of the debt.

Third-Party Pawn and Absconding Slave: Two Rulings in Rahn
Two rulings from nawadir: third-party pawn sequence and absconding slave's defect reducing debt.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a third-party pawn without debtor's permission and explain how the debt is allocated, and also explain the effect of a pawned slave's absconding on the debt.

Core Idea
A third-party pawn is valid; the first covers the full debt, subsequent pawns share the remainder. An absconding slave reduces the debt by the defect's value.

This lesson delves into two specific rulings from the Hanafi nawadir: the case of an 'ajnabi (third party) pawning his property for another's debt without permission, and the case of a pawned slave that runs away. Both illustrate how the legal principle of pawn (rahn) interacts with the nature of the debt and the condition of the collateral. By understanding these, you will grasp how Hanafi jurists reason about security and defects.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two distinct legal questions
The passage presents two separate rulings. The first concerns multiple third-party pawns on the same debt; the second concerns a defect (absconding) in the pawned item. Treat each as its own case.
2
Analyze the third-party pawn sequence
When two different third parties each pawn a slave without the debtor's order, the first pawn covers the entire debt because no prior pawn encumbered the debt. The second pawn only covers the remaining half because a pawn already exists on the debt.
Reasoning: 'first is subordinate in the pawn and there is no pawn upon the debt' (al-awwal taba' bi al-rahn wa la rahn bi al-dain).
3
Analyze the absconding slave case
A pawned slave that absconds and is later found becomes defective; his value decreases. The debt is reduced by the amount of that decrease because the pawn serves as security for the debt.
Principle: 'by absconding he became defective' (li-annahu bi al-ibaq sara ma'iban). The diminution in value directly reduces the secured debt.
4
Note the authority and transmission level
These rulings come from the nawadir (rare transmissions): the first from Hisham reporting from Muhammad al-Shaybani; the second from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad reporting from Abu Hanifa. They are not from the six core books (Zahir al-Riwayah) but are still valid positions.
Authority weight: nawadir. Cross-madhhab: mukhtalaf fih.
5
Reflect on the underlying legal principles
Both rulings rest on the idea that the pawn is subordinate to the debt (al-rahn tabi' li al-dain). The pawn's value is a security, and its condition directly affects the claim. For the third-party pawn, the sequence matters because the debt can only be secured once fully; for the defect, the security diminishes proportionally.
These are applications of the general rule that the pawn covers the debt up to its value, and any decrease in value due to the pawn's own actions reduces the debt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال في المنتقى : روى هشام عن محمد: رهن أجنبي بدين ألف عبداً بغير أمر المطلوب ثم أجنبي آخر رهنه عبداً آخر بغير أمر المطلوب فهو جائز والأول رهن بألف والثاني رهن بخمسمائة لأن الأول تبع بالرهن ولا رهن بالدين فيكون رهناً بجميع الدين، والثاني رهن وبالدين رهن فلا يصير رهناً إلا بخمسمائة . وذكر الحسن عن أبي حنيفة : إذا أبق العبد الرهن ثم وجد بطل من الدين بقدر نقصان الآبق لأنه بالاباق صار معيباً فإنه لا يشتري بعد الإباق بمثل ما يشتري قبل
He said in al-Muntaqa: Hisham reported from Muhammad: An alien pawned a slave for a debt of a thousand without the order of the person sought (the debtor), then another alien pawned another slave for the same debt without order: it is permissible. The first is a pawn for a thousand, and the second is a pawn for five hundred, because the first is subordinate in the pawn and there is no pawn upon the debt, so it becomes a pawn for the entire debt. The second is a pawn and the debt is pawned? Actually: 'the second is a pawn and upon the debt there is a pawn' so it only becomes a pawn for five hundred. And al-Hasan reported from Abu Hanifa: If the pawned slave absconds and then is found, the debt is reduced by the measure of the defect of the absconding, because by absconding he became defective, for he is not bought after absconding like he is bought before.
Source pages p. 516

Commentary
This passage presents two independent rulings from earlier Hanafi authorities. The first ruling comes from al-Muntaqa, citing Hisham from Muhammad (al-Shaybani). It deals with a third party ('ajnabi) who pawns a slave without the debtor's order. If two different third parties each pawn a slave for the same debt, the first pawn covers the full debt (1000), but the second only covers half (500). The reasoning: the first pawn becomes subordinate to the debt—meaning the slave is security for the entire debt. Since there is no existing pawn on the debt when the first is made, it covers all. When the second pawn is made, there is already a pawn covering the debt, so the second slave only becomes a pawn for the remaining half. The second ruling is from al-Hasan (ibn Ziyad) reporting from Abu Hanifa on the case of a pawned slave that absconds (abqa). When the slave runs away and is later found, his value has decreased due to the defect of absconding (since buyers will pay less). The debt is reduced by the amount of that decrease. This is because the pawn is security for the debt, and if its value diminishes due to a defect caused by the slave's own actions (absconding), the debt reduces proportionally.

Key Terms
أجنبي (ajnabi): A third party who is not the debtor nor the creditor. He pawns his own property to secure someone else's debt without the debtor's permission.
الإباق (al-ibaq): Absconding or running away of a slave. It is considered a defect that reduces the slave's value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man pawns his slave to secure a friend's debt of 1000 dirhams without the friend's permission. Later, another man pawns another slave for the same debt without permission. How much debt does each pawn cover?
A) Both pawns cover 1000 dirhams each.
B) The first covers 1000, the second covers 500.
C) The first covers 500, the second covers 500.
D) Neither is valid without the debtor's permission.

Key Takeaway
A third-party pawn is valid in Hanafi law; the first pawn covers the entire debt, and subsequent pawns split the remainder; a defect in the pawn due to the pawn's own actions (like absconding) reduces the debt proportionally.

The Increase of a Pawn: Ownership and Pawn Status
Commentary on the matn: the increase (offspring, fruit, etc.) belongs to the pledgor and is also pawned

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the increase (nama') of a pawned asset and explain why the increase is also subject to the pawn and how it is redeemed if the original perishes.

Core Idea
The increase of a pawn belongs to the pledgor but is also pawned; if the original perishes, the increase is redeemed by its share of the debt.

In the contract of pawn (rahn), the pledged asset may produce offspring, fruit, or other forms of increase. This lesson explores the legal status of such increase in the Hanafi school. We will learn that the increase is considered a follower (taba') of the original, so it is automatically included in the pawn. However, ownership remains with the pledgor. A key consequence is that if the original perishes, the increase becomes the primary object of redemption and is released upon payment of its proportional share of the debt.

Guided Path
1
Identify who owns the increase
The passage begins by stating that the increase (offspring, fruit, milk, wool) belongs to the pledgor because it is generated from his property. This establishes ownership despite the pawn.
The increase does not become the property of the mortgagee; it remains owned by the pledgor.
2
Understand that the increase is also pawned
The commentator explains that the pawn right is strong and binding, and it extends (yasri) to the increase as a follower. Therefore, the increase is also subject to the pawn contract without needing separate mention.
This follows the principle of taba'iyya (followership) in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Examine contrasts with other contexts
The text compares the pawn to cases where offspring does not follow the mother's legal status: a female slave against whom a crime is committed, a leased slave, a guarantor's slave, a usurped slave, and a slave bequeathed for service. In each, the right is weaker or different, so the offspring is not automatically included.
These contrasts highlight the strength and comprehensive nature of the pawn right.
4
Learn the consequence if the increase perishes
If the increase itself perishes while the original remains, it is lost without compensation (majanan). The reason is that the increase entered the contract only as a follower and was not explicitly intended; thus, it carries no independent countervalue.
The mortgagee does not owe anything for the lost increase, and the debt remains unchanged.
5
Apply the rule when the original perishes and the increase remains
If the original pawned asset perishes but the increase survives, the increase now becomes the intended object of redemption. It is redeemed for its share of the debt, analogous to the offspring of a sold slave when the mother dies before delivery.
The passage uses a qiyas (analogy) to the sale case to justify the proportional redemption.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وإنماء الرهن كالولد والتمر واللبن والصوف للراهن لأنه متولد من ملكه. قال رحمه الله: (وهو رهن مع الأصل) وهو تبع له والرهن حق متأكد لازم يسري إلى الولد ألا ترى أن الراهن لا يملك به إبطاله بخلاف ولد الجارية حيث لا يسري حكم الجناية إلى الولد ولا يتبع لأنه فيها غير متأكد حتى ينفرد المالك بإبطاله بالفداء بخلاف ولد المستأجرة والكفيلة والمغصوبة وولد الموصي بخدمتها لأن المستأجر حقه في المنفعة دون العين وفي الكفالة الحق يثبت في الذمة والولد لا يتولد من الذمة وفي الغصب إثبات اليد العادية بإزالة اليد المحقة وهو معدوم في الولد ولا يمكن إثباته فيه تبعاً لأنه فعل حسي والتبعية لا تجري في الأوصاف الشرعية، وفي الجارية الموصى بخدمتها المستحق له الخدمة وهي منفعة الأم والولد غير صالح لها قبل الانفصال فلا يكون تبعاً، وبعده لا ينقلب موجباً أيضاً بعد أن انعقد غير موجب . قال رحمه الله : ( ويهلك مجاناً) أي إذا هلك النماء يهلك مجاناً بغير شيء لأن الاتباع لا قسط لها مما يتقابل بالأصل لأنها لم تدخل تحت العقد مقصوداً. قال رحمه الله : (وإن هلك الأصل وبقي النماء فك بحصته) يعني إذا هلك الأصل وهو الرهن وبقي النماء وهو الولد يفتك الولد بحصته من الدين لأنه صار مقصوداً بالفكاك والنماء إذا صار مقصوداً بالفكاك يكون له قسط كولد المبيع لا حصة له من الثمن، ثم إذا صار مقصوداً بالقبض صار له حصة حتى لو هلكت الأم قبل القبض وبقي الولد كان للمشتري أن يأخذه بحصته من الثمن، ولو هلك قبل القبض
أمه فيه
He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: 'And the increase of the pledge, like offspring, dates, milk, and wool, belongs to the pledgor because it is generated from his property.' He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: 'And it is a pledge with the original.' That is, it is a follower of it. The pledge is a strong, binding right that permeates to the offspring. Do you not see that the pledgor does not have the power to annul it? Unlike the offspring of a female slave (against whom a crime is committed), where the ruling of the crime does not permeate to the offspring and it does not follow, because it is not strong in that case, so the owner is alone in annulling it by ransom. Unlike the offspring of a leased (female slave), a guarantor, a usurped (female slave), and the offspring of a female slave bequeathed for service, because the lessee's right is in benefit not the substance, in guarantee the right is established in the debt and the offspring is not generated from the debt, in usurpation the establishment of the tortious hand by removing the legitimate hand does not exist in the offspring and cannot be established in it as a follower because it is a physical act and followership does not apply in legal descriptions. In the female slave bequeathed for service, the entitled person has the service, which is a benefit of the mother, and the offspring is not suitable for it before separation, so it does not follow, and after it, it does not become a cause either, after having been established as not a cause. He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: 'And it perishes for free.' That is, if the increase perishes, it perishes gratuitously without anything, because the followership has no share from what corresponds to the original, since it did not enter the contract as an intended object. He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: 'And if the original perishes and the increase remains, it is redeemed by its share.' That is, if the original, which is the pawn, perishes and the increase, which is the offspring, remains, the offspring is redeemed for its share of the debt because it has become intended by redemption. And the increase, when it becomes intended by redemption, has a share, like the offspring of a sold (slave) has no share of the price initially, but when it becomes intended by delivery, it has a share. So if the mother perishes before delivery and the offspring remains, the buyer may take it for its share of the price. And if it perishes before delivery, its mother is in it? (The text cuts off).
Source pages p. 516

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq regarding the increase (nama') of a pawned asset. The ruling: the offspring, fruit, milk, and wool generated from a pawned item belong to the pledgor (since they are produced from his property), but they are also subject to the pawn along with the original (the principal pawned asset). The commentator explains that the pawn is a strong, binding right that extends (yasri) to the offspring. He illustrates this by contrasting it with other contexts where offspring does not follow the mother's legal status. For example, if a pawned female slave is injured, the offspring is not automatically pawned because the pawn right is not strong enough to extend to a future entity? Actually, the contrast is with the offspring of a female slave for whom blood money is due (jirah): the ruling of the crime does not extend to the offspring. Similarly, offspring of a leased slave, a guarantor's slave, a usurped slave, and a slave bequeathed for service do not follow the mother's pawn because the rights there are weaker or different in nature. The commentator also explains the principle that if the increase perishes, it does so without compensation (majanan) because it is only a follower and was not explicitly intended in the pawn contract. However, if the original perishes and the increase survives, the increase now becomes the primary object of redemption and is redeemed for its proportional share of the debt. The analogy is made to the offspring of a sold slave: initially, the offspring has no share in the price, but if the mother dies before delivery, the buyer can take the offspring for its share of the price. The commentary provides a detailed legal reasoning grounded in the nature of rights (followership, strength of the pawn, etc.).

Key Terms
النماء (an-nama'): Increase or growth generated from the pawned asset, such as offspring of animals, fruit of trees, milk, wool, etc.
التبع (at-taba'): Followership; the legal status of the increase as dependent on the principal pawned asset.
الفكاك (al-fikak): Redemption; the release of the pawned item (or its increase) by payment of the debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if the increase of a pawn perishes (e.g., the lamb dies), what is the legal consequence?
A) The mortgagee must compensate the pledgor.
B) The pledgor must compensate the mortgagee.
C) It perishes without compensation (majanan).
D) The debt is reduced by the value of the increase.

Key Takeaway
The increase of a pawn belongs to the pledgor but is automatically included in the pawn; if the original is lost, the increase is redeemed for its share of the debt.

The Offspring of a Pawn: Ownership and Pledge Status
Establishes the basic rulings for the offspring of a pawn.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the basic Hanafi ruling regarding the ownership of the offspring of a pawned item and explain its status as part of the pledge.

Core Idea
The offspring of a pawn belongs to the pledgor, is part of the pledge, and perishes gratuitously.

When a pawned item produces offspring or increments like milk or wool, a natural question arises: who owns these increments and what is their legal status regarding the debt? This lesson lays down the fundamental rule from the Hanafi matn and its commentary, clarifying that the pledgor retains ownership but the increment becomes part of the pledged security.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State what the offspring (inma') of a pawn is and who owns it according to the matn.
The matn says 'لِلرَّاهِنِ' (belongs to the pledgor).
2
Explain the pledge status
Understand that the offspring is 'رهن مع الأصل' (a pledge with the original). It is automatically part of the security.
It is a dependent (tabi') of the original pledge.
3
Understand gratuitous loss
If the offspring perishes on its own, it is a loss to the pledgor without compensation from the mortgagee.
The matn says 'ويهلك مجاناً' (perishes gratuitously).
4
Learn redemption if the original perishes
If the original pawn perishes but the offspring remains, the offspring can be redeemed by paying a share of the debt proportional to its value.
The matn says 'فك بحصته' (redeemed by its share).

الدين ربعه وهو مائتان وخمسون لأن الدين ينقسم عليهما نصفين فيذهب نصف ما كان فيها من الدين وفي المنتقى رهن أرضاً ونخلاً بدين قيمة كل واحد خمسمائة فاحترق النخل ونبت في الأرض نخل آخر يساوي خمسمائة قال : يذهب من الدين نصفه باحتراق النخل وما نبت فهو زيادة في الأرض بمنزلة رجل رهن أمتين فماتت إحداهما ثم ولدت الباقية جارية بألف فقتلتها أمة تساوي مائة فدفعت بها ثم ولدت ولداً يساوي ألفاً فالدين بينهما نصفان لأن الأمة الأولى على حالها والزيادة في الرهن حكمها حكم الأصل محبوسة مضمونة كالأصل لأنها تلحق بأصل العقد وصارت كالموجودة في العقد كما في زوائد المبيع. ويقسم الدين على قيمة الأصل يوم القبض، وعلى قيمة الزيادة يوم قبضت، فإن كانت قيمة الأصل وقيمة الزيادة يوم قبضت خمسمائة انقسم الدين عليهما أثلاثاً لأن الضمان إنما يجب بالقبض فتعتبر قيمة كل واحد منهما يوم القبض، فإن نقص الرهن في يده ثم زاد آخر قسم ما بقي من الدين على قيمة الباقي وقيمة الزيادة يوم قبضت مثاله : إذا رهن عبداً يساوي ألفاً بألف فاعور ثم زاده رهناً آخر قسم ما بقي من الدين على قيمة الباقي وهو العبد الأعور وعلى قيمة العبد الزائد أثلاثاً، ثلثه بإزاء العبد القديم وثلثاه بإزاء العبد الزائد بخلاف ما إذا ولدت :
The end and it is the Book of Pledge, Chapter of Disposition in the Pledge and Injury upon it and its Injury upon others. With a dirham. And the growth of the pledge like the child, dates, milk, and wool belongs to the pledgor, and it is a pledge with the original, and it perishes gratuitously. And if the original perishes and the growth remains, it is redeemed by its share, and the debt is divided according to its value on the day... because the [؟] did not cease from the meat, and the remainder of the debt was six, so the skin became pawned for six, guaranteed for a dirham, because every part of the sheep is pawned for the entire debt, guaranteed to the measure of its value, so likewise the skin. This is if it is tanned with something of no value. But if it is tanned with something of value, then the mortgagee is entitled to detainment for the increase of the tanning, like usurpation. So if detainment is due for another new debt, does the first pledge become void? The jurist Abu Ja'far al-Hinduwani, may Allah have mercy on him, said: One might say that the first pledge becomes void regarding the skin and the skin becomes a pledge for the increase of the tanning, as if the pledgor pawned this object for a new debt. And one might say that the first pledge remains and it becomes detained for the value of the tanning, so that the pledgor cannot redeem it unless he pays what is against it of the debt and the value of the tanning. He said in al-Muntaqa: Hisham narrated from Muhammad: A stranger pawned a slave for a debt of a thousand without the order of the debtor, then another stranger pawned another slave without the order of the debtor. It is permissible. The first is a pledge for a thousand, and the second is a pledge for five hundred, because the first is a pledge and there is no debt in the pledge, so it becomes a pledge for the entire debt. The second is a pledge and the debt is a pledge, so it does not become a pledge except for five hundred. And al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa: If the pawned slave runs away and then is found, the debt is remitted by the amount of the deficiency of the runaway, because by running away it became defective, for it is not bought after running away for what it was bought before. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And the growth of the pledge like the child, dates, milk, and wool belongs to the pledgor) because it is generated from his property. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And it is a pledge with the original) and it is a dependent of it. A pledge is an established, binding right that extends to the child. Do you not see that the pledgor cannot invalidate it, unlike the child of the female slave, where the ruling of injury does not extend to the child, nor does it follow, because in it [the pledge] it is not established, such that the owner can invalidate it by ransom, unlike the child of the leased female slave, the guarantor, the usurped, and the one whose service is bequeathed, because the lessee's right is in the usufruct, not the substance; in guarantee, the right is established in the liability, and the child is not generated from the liability; in usurpation, it is establishing a tortious hand by removing a rightful hand, and that is absent in the child and cannot be established in it as a dependent because it is a physical act, and dependency does not run in legal descriptions; and in the female slave whose service is bequeathed, the one entitled to service has a right to the usufruct of the mother, and the child is not suitable for it before separation, so it is not a dependent, and after it, it does not become a cause either after it was not a cause. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And it perishes gratuitously) i.e., if the growth perishes, it perishes gratuitously for nothing, because dependency has no share in what is exchanged with the original, because it did not enter the contract as an intended object. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And if the original perishes and the growth remains, it is redeemed by its share) meaning if the original, which is the pledge, perishes and the growth, which is the child, remains, the child is redeemed by its share of the debt, because it has become an intended object of redemption. When the growth becomes an intended object of redemption, it has a share, like the child of a sold item has no share of the price; but when it becomes an intended object of receipt, it gets a share. So if the mother perishes before receipt and the child remains, the buyer may take it by its share of the price. And if it perishes before receipt, the mother [is] in it. The redemption and the value of the original on the day of receipt, and the share of the original falls from the debt, and the growth is redeemed by its share. Nothing of the price falls. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And the debt is divided according to its value.) The redemption and the value of the original on the day of receipt, and the share of the original falls from the debt, and the growth is redeemed by its share, because the child got a share by redemption on the day the mother entered into liability at the time of receipt, so the value of each of them at the time of its consideration is considered. For this reason, if the child perishes after the mother's death but before redemption, it perishes for nothing, so it is known that nothing of the debt corresponds to it except at redemption. And if the pledgor authorizes the mortgagee to consume the increments of the pledge by saying, "Whatever increases, consume it," then there is no liability on him, and nothing drops from the pledge because he destroyed it with the pledgor's permission. This is a permission (ibaha), and the absolute permission is allowed to be suspended on a condition and risk, unlike transfer of ownership. If he does not redeem the pledge until it perishes in the mortgagee's hand, the debt is divided over the value of the increment that the mortgagee consumed, and upon him is the value of the original. Whatever corresponds to the original falls, and whatever corresponds to the increment, the mortgagee takes from the pledgor, because the increment perished in the pledgor's property by the mortgagee's action with his authorization, so it is as if the pledgor took and destroyed it, and it is guaranteed against him, so he has the debt. This is mentioned in al-Hidayah and al-Kafi. And in Fatawa Qadikhan and al-Muhit, and attributed to al-Jami': If the value of the mother decreases due to a change in market price and becomes five hundred, or increases and becomes two thousand, while the child remains as it is valued at a thousand, then the debt is divided between them in halves and does not change from what it was. If the mother remains as it is and the value of the child decreases due to a defect or a change in market price and becomes five hundred, then the debt is divided between them into thirds: two-thirds in the mother and one-third in the child. If the value of the child increases to become two thousand, then two-thirds of the debt is in the child and one-third in the mother, so that if the mother perishes, the child remains with two-thirds of the debt. If the mother gives birth to a child and their values are equal, then the mother becomes one-eyed after birth or before, one-fourth of the debt goes, which is two hundred and fifty, because the debt is divided between them in halves, so half of what was in her of the debt goes. And in al-Muntaqa: He pawned land and palm trees for a debt, the value of each being five hundred. The palm trees burned, and other palm trees grew in the land worth five hundred. He said: Half of the debt goes by the burning of the palm trees, and what grew is an increase in the land... like a man who pawned two slave girls, then one of them died, then the remaining one gave birth to a slave girl worth a thousand, then a female slave [worth] a hundred killed her and she was given in compensation, then she gave birth to a child worth a thousand. The debt is divided between them in halves, because the first slave girl remains as she was, and the increase in the pledge has the same ruling as the original, detained and guaranteed like the original, because it is attached to the original contract and becomes as if present in the contract, as in the increments of a sold item. The debt is divided according to the value of the original on the day of receipt and the value of the increase on the day it was received. If the value of the original and the value of the increase on the day it was received were five hundred, the debt is divided between them into thirds, because liability is only obligated by receipt, so the value of each of them on the day of receipt is considered. If the pledge decreases [in value] in his hand, then he adds another pledge, what remains of the debt is divided over the value of the remaining and the value of the increase on the day it was received. Example: If he pawned a slave worth a thousand for a thousand, then he became one-eyed, then he added another pledge, what remains of the debt is divided over the value of the remaining, which is the one-eyed slave, and the value of the added slave into thirds: one-third against the old slave and two-thirds against the added slave, contrary to if she gave birth:
Source pages p. 516

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq (The Full Moon) is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq by Imam al-Nasafi. It discusses the rulings regarding the offspring (inma') or increments produced by a pawned item (rahn). The passage begins with the fundamental rule: the offspring of a pawn, such as a child, dates, milk, and wool, belong to the pledgor (rahin) because they are generated from his property. However, these increments are also part of the pawn itself, meaning they are pledged along with the original asset. If the increment perishes on its own, the pledgor bears the loss without any compensation from the mortgagee (murtahin). If the original pawn perishes but the increment remains, the increment can be redeemed by paying a proportional share of the debt. The debt is divided based on the value of the original and the increment at the time of receipt (qabd). The passage provides a detailed example involving the skin of a sheep: the skin, after the meat is consumed, becomes a pawn for the remaining debt, and it is guaranteed for its value. The discussion then moves to a special case: if the skin is tanned with a substance of value, the mortgagee gains a right to detain the skin for the additional value created by the tanning, similar to the ruling on usurpation (ghasb). This raises a question: does the new right invalidate the original pledge? Two views are presented: one that the original pledge becomes void regarding the skin, making it a new pledge for the tanning value, and another that the original pledge remains but the skin is detained for the tanning value. The text then narrates a report from al-Muntaqa via Hisham ibn Muhammad: if two strangers pawn the same debtor's items without his order, the first becomes a pledge for the entire debt while the second is only pledge for half, due to the principle that the pledge is a surety for the debt, and the second pledge is shared with the first debt. Another report from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad quotes Abu Hanifa on a runaway slave: if the pawned slave runs away and is found, the debt is reduced proportionally because the slave's value has decreased. The commentary then unpacks the matn phrase by phrase. It explains why the offspring is a dependent (tabi') of the original pledge, using analogies and distinctions with other cases like the child of a leased female slave, a guarantor, a usurped item, or a bequeathed usufruct. The dependency means the offspring does not have an independent share in the redemption unless it becomes an intended object (maqsud) when the original is lost. The commentary also addresses the scenario where the pledgor authorizes the mortgagee to consume the increments: the mortgagee is not liable, and the debt is not reduced. If the pledge perishes after consumption, the debt is divided, and the mortgagee takes the value of the consumed increment from the pledgor. Later sections discuss changes in value due to market fluctuations or defects. For example, if the mother's value changes but the child remains, the debt division adjusts proportionally. Detailed calculations are given for various scenarios, emphasizing that the division is based on values at the time of receipt. The passage concludes with an example from al-Muntaqa about pawned land and palms, and another about two female slaves, illustrating how increases are treated as part of the pledge. The overall lesson is that the offspring and other increments of a pawn are governed by the same ruling as the original, but with specific rules for redemption, loss, and division of debt.

Key Terms
إنماء الرهن (inma' al-rahn): The growth or increment produced by a pawned item, such as offspring, milk, wool, or fruit.
رهن (rahn): A pawn or pledge: an item given as security for a debt.
فك (fakk): Redemption: releasing the pledge by paying the debt or a portion thereof.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is true about the offspring of a pawned item in Hanafi fiqh?
A) It belongs to the mortgagee.
B) It belongs to the pledgor and is part of the pledge.
C) It belongs to the pledgor but is not part of the pledge.
D) Its ownership is suspended until the debt is paid.

Key Takeaway
The offspring of a pawn is owned by the pledgor, serves as additional security, perishes without compensation, and is redeemed proportionally if the original is lost.

Tanning the Skin: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on New Pledge
Presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the effect of tanning with valuable substance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two conflicting Hanafi views on whether tanning a pawned skin with a valuable substance creates a new pledge or preserves the original.

Core Idea
Tanning a pawned skin with valuable substance creates a new security interest, but scholars differ on whether it invalidates the original pledge.

The previous lesson assumed the tanning substance had no value. But what if the tanning material is valuable? Does the added value create a separate pledge, and does it affect the original pledge? Al-Hinduwani reports two possible views within the Hanafi school, rooted in analogical reasoning. This lesson analyzes that intra-madhhab dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the new condition
Note that the ruling changes when the tanning substance has value. The mortgagee gains a right of detention for the added value.
The text says 'يستحق المرتهن الحبس بما زاد الدباغ فيه'
2
State the first view (new pledge)
One possible view: the first pledge becomes void regarding the skin, and the skin becomes a new pledge for the tanning value.
Analogy: if the pledgor pawns the same item for a new debt.
3
State the second view (continued pledge)
The alternative view: the first pledge remains, and the skin is detained for the tanning value without voiding the original.
The pledgor cannot redeem the skin without paying both the original debt and the tanning value.
4
Analyze the practical consequence (thamarah)
The difference affects how much the pledgor must pay to release the skin.
First view: pay only the tanning value for the skin (original debt is separate). Second view: pay both.
