آخر وهو كتاب الرهن باب التصرف في الرهن والجناية عليه وجنايته على غيره بدرهم وإنماء الرهن كالولد والتمر واللبن والصوف للراهن وهو رهن مع الأصل ويهلك مجاناً وإن هلك الأصل وبقي النماء فك بحصته ويقسم الدين على قيمته يوم لأنه لم يزل التوى عن اللحم وكان الباقي من الدين ستة فصار الجلد مرهوناً بستة مضموناً بدرهم لأن كل جزء من أجزاء الشاة مرهون بجميع الدين مضمون بمقدار قيمته فكذا الجلد. هذا إذا دبغ بشيء لا قيمة له، فإن دبغ بشيء له قيمة فإنه يستحق المرتهن الحبس بما زاد الدباغ فيه كالغصب، فإذا استحق الحبس بدين آخر حادث هل يبطل الرهن الأول؟ قال الفقيه أبو جعفر الهندواني رحمه الله تعالى : لقائل أن يقول يبطل الرهن الأول في حق الجلد ويصير الجلد رهناً بما زاد الدباغ فيه كما لو رهن الراهن هذه العين بدين حادث، ولقائل أن يقول يبقى الرهن الأول ويصير محبوساً بقيمة الدباغ حتى لا يكون للراهن أن يفتكه ما لم يرد ما بإزائه من الدين وقيمة الدباغ قال في المنتقى : روى هشام عن محمد: رهن أجنبي بدين ألف عبداً بغير أمر المطلوب ثم أجنبي آخر رهنه عبداً آخر بغير أمر المطلوب فهو جائز والأول رهن بألف والثاني رهن بخمسمائة لأن الأول تبع بالرهن ولا رهن بالدين فيكون رهناً بجميع الدين، والثاني رهن وبالدين رهن فلا يصير رهناً إلا بخمسمائة . وذكر الحسن عن أبي حنيفة : إذا أبق العبد الرهن ثم وجد بطل من الدين بقدر نقصان الآبق لأنه بالاباق صار معيباً فإنه لا يشتري بعد الإباق بمثل ما يشتري قبله قال رحمه الله : (وإنماء الرهن كالولد والتمر واللبن والصوف للراهن لأنه متولد من ملكه. قال رحمه الله: (وهو رهن مع الأصل) وهو تبع له والرهن حق متأكد لازم يسري إلى الولد ألا ترى أن الراهن لا يملك به إبطاله بخلاف ولد الجارية حيث لا يسري حكم الجناية إلى الولد ولا يتبع لأنه فيها غير متأكد حتى ينفرد المالك بإبطاله بالفداء بخلاف ولد المستأجرة والكفيلة والمغصوبة وولد الموصي بخدمتها لأن المستأجر حقه في المنفعة دون العين وفي الكفالة الحق يثبت في الذمة والولد لا يتولد من الذمة وفي الغصب إثبات اليد العادية بإزالة اليد المحقة وهو معدوم في الولد ولا يمكن إثباته فيه تبعاً لأنه فعل حسي والتبعية لا تجري في الأوصاف الشرعية، وفي الجارية الموصى بخدمتها المستحق له الخدمة وهي منفعة الأم والولد غير صالح لها قبل الانفصال فلا يكون تبعاً، وبعده لا ينقلب موجباً أيضاً بعد أن انعقد غير موجب . قال رحمه الله : ( ويهلك مجاناً) أي إذا هلك النماء يهلك مجاناً بغير شيء لأن الاتباع لا قسط لها مما يتقابل بالأصل لأنها لم تدخل تحت العقد مقصوداً. قال رحمه الله : (وإن هلك الأصل وبقي النماء فك بحصته) يعني إذا هلك الأصل وهو الرهن وبقي النماء وهو الولد يفتك الولد بحصته من الدين لأنه صار مقصوداً بالفكاك والنماء إذا صار مقصوداً بالفكاك يكون له قسط كولد المبيع لا حصة له من الثمن، ثم إذا صار مقصوداً بالقبض صار له حصة حتى لو هلكت الأم قبل القبض وبقي الولد كان للمشتري أن يأخذه بحصته من الثمن، ولو هلك قبل القبض أمه فيه الفكاك وقيمة الأصل يوم القبض وسقط من الدين حصة الأصل وفك النماء بحصته لا يسقط شيء من الثمن . قال رحمه الله : (ويقسم الدين على قيمته . الفكاك وقيمة الأصل يوم القبض وسقط من الدين حصة الأصل وفك النماء بحصته لأن الولد صار له حصة بالفكاك يوم والأم دخلت في الضمان وقت القبض فيعتبر قيمة كل واحد منهما في وقت اعتباره، ولهذا من لو هلك الولد بعد هلاك أمه قبل الفكاك هلك بغير شيء فيعلم بذلك أنه لا يقابله شيء من الدين إلا عند الفكاك . ولو أذن الراهن للمرتهن في أكل زوائد الرهن بأن قال مهما زاد فكله فلا ضمان عليه ولا يسقط شيء من الرهن لأنه أتلفه بإذن الراهن وهذه إباحة والإطلاق يجوز تعليقه بالشرط والخطر بخلاف التمليك، وإن لم يفتك الرهن حتى هلك في يد المرتهن قسم الدين على قيمة الزيادة التي أكلها المرتهن وعليه قيمة الأصل فما أصاب الأصل سقط، وما أصاب الزيادة أخذه المرتهن من الراهن لأن الزيادة تلفت على ملك الراهن بفعل المرتهن بتسليط منه فصار كأن الراهن أخذه وأتلفه ويكون مضموناً عليه فكان له الدين؛ هكذا ذكره في الهداية والكافي. وفي فتاوى قاضيخان والمحيط وعزاه إلى الجامع : ولو نقصت قيمة الأم بتغير السعر فصارت تساوي خمسمائة أو زادت فصارت تساوي ألفين والولد على حاله يساوي ألفاً فالدين بينهما نصفان ولا يتغير عما كان، وإن كانت الأم على حالها وانتقصت قيمة الولد بعيب . أو بتغير السعر فصارت خمسمائة فالدين بينهما أثلاثاً ثلثان في الأم والثلث في الولد، ولو زادت قيمة الولد فصار يساوي ألفين فثلثا الدين في الولد والثلث في الأم حتى لو هلكت الأم بقي الولد بثلثي الدين. ولو ولدت الأم ولداً وقيمتهما سواء ثم اعورت الأم بعد الولادة أو قبلها ذهب من الدين ربعه وهو مائتان وخمسون لأن الدين ينقسم عليهما نصفين فيذهب نصف ما كان فيها من الدين وفي المنتقى رهن أرضاً ونخلاً بدين قيمة كل واحد خمسمائة فاحترق النخل ونبت في الأرض نخل آخر يساوي خمسمائة قال : يذهب من الدين نصفه باحتراق النخل وما نبت فهو زيادة في الأرض بمنزلة رجل رهن أمتين فماتت إحداهما ثم ولدت الباقية جارية بألف فقتلتها أمة تساوي مائة فدفعت بها ثم ولدت ولداً يساوي ألفاً فالدين بينهما نصفان لأن الأمة الأولى على حالها والزيادة في الرهن حكمها حكم الأصل محبوسة مضمونة كالأصل لأنها تلحق بأصل العقد وصارت كالموجودة في العقد كما في زوائد المبيع. ويقسم الدين على قيمة الأصل يوم القبض، وعلى قيمة الزيادة يوم قبضت، فإن كانت قيمة الأصل وقيمة الزيادة يوم قبضت خمسمائة انقسم الدين عليهما أثلاثاً لأن الضمان إنما يجب بالقبض فتعتبر قيمة كل واحد منهما يوم القبض، فإن نقص الرهن في يده ثم زاد آخر قسم ما بقي من الدين على قيمة الباقي وقيمة الزيادة يوم قبضت مثاله : إذا رهن عبداً يساوي ألفاً بألف فاعور ثم زاده رهناً آخر قسم ما بقي من الدين على قيمة الباقي وهو العبد الأعور وعلى قيمة العبد الزائد أثلاثاً، ثلثه بإزاء العبد القديم وثلثاه بإزاء العبد الزائد بخلاف ما إذا ولدت :
The end and it is the Book of Pledge, Chapter of Disposition in the Pledge and Injury upon it and its Injury upon others. With a dirham. And the growth of the pledge like the child, dates, milk, and wool belongs to the pledgor, and it is a pledge with the original, and it perishes gratuitously. And if the original perishes and the growth remains, it is redeemed by its share, and the debt is divided according to its value on the day... because the [؟] did not cease from the meat, and the remainder of the debt was six, so the skin became pawned for six, guaranteed for a dirham, because every part of the sheep is pawned for the entire debt, guaranteed to the measure of its value, so likewise the skin. This is if it is tanned with something of no value. But if it is tanned with something of value, then the mortgagee is entitled to detainment for the increase of the tanning, like usurpation. So if detainment is due for another new debt, does the first pledge become void? The jurist Abu Ja'far al-Hinduwani, may Allah have mercy on him, said: One might say that the first pledge becomes void regarding the skin and the skin becomes a pledge for the increase of the tanning, as if the pledgor pawned this object for a new debt. And one might say that the first pledge remains and it becomes detained for the value of the tanning, so that the pledgor cannot redeem it unless he pays what is against it of the debt and the value of the tanning. He said in al-Muntaqa: Hisham narrated from Muhammad: A stranger pawned a slave for a debt of a thousand without the order of the debtor, then another stranger pawned another slave without the order of the debtor. It is permissible. The first is a pledge for a thousand, and the second is a pledge for five hundred, because the first is a pledge and there is no debt in the pledge, so it becomes a pledge for the entire debt. The second is a pledge and the debt is a pledge, so it does not become a pledge except for five hundred. And al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa: If the pawned slave runs away and then is found, the debt is remitted by the amount of the deficiency of the runaway, because by running away it became defective, for it is not bought after running away for what it was bought before. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And the growth of the pledge like the child, dates, milk, and wool belongs to the pledgor) because it is generated from his property. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And it is a pledge with the original) and it is a dependent of it. A pledge is an established, binding right that extends to the child. Do you not see that the pledgor cannot invalidate it, unlike the child of the female slave, where the ruling of injury does not extend to the child, nor does it follow, because in it [the pledge] it is not established, such that the owner can invalidate it by ransom, unlike the child of the leased female slave, the guarantor, the usurped, and the one whose service is bequeathed, because the lessee's right is in the usufruct, not the substance; in guarantee, the right is established in the liability, and the child is not generated from the liability; in usurpation, it is establishing a tortious hand by removing a rightful hand, and that is absent in the child and cannot be established in it as a dependent because it is a physical act, and dependency does not run in legal descriptions; and in the female slave whose service is bequeathed, the one entitled to service has a right to the usufruct of the mother, and the child is not suitable for it before separation, so it is not a dependent, and after it, it does not become a cause either after it was not a cause. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And it perishes gratuitously) i.e., if the growth perishes, it perishes gratuitously for nothing, because dependency has no share in what is exchanged with the original, because it did not enter the contract as an intended object. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And if the original perishes and the growth remains, it is redeemed by its share) meaning if the original, which is the pledge, perishes and the growth, which is the child, remains, the child is redeemed by its share of the debt, because it has become an intended object of redemption. When the growth becomes an intended object of redemption, it has a share, like the child of a sold item has no share of the price; but when it becomes an intended object of receipt, it gets a share. So if the mother perishes before receipt and the child remains, the buyer may take it by its share of the price. And if it perishes before receipt, the mother [is] in it. The redemption and the value of the original on the day of receipt, and the share of the original falls from the debt, and the growth is redeemed by its share. Nothing of the price falls. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And the debt is divided according to its value.) The redemption and the value of the original on the day of receipt, and the share of the original falls from the debt, and the growth is redeemed by its share, because the child got a share by redemption on the day the mother entered into liability at the time of receipt, so the value of each of them at the time of its consideration is considered. For this reason, if the child perishes after the mother's death but before redemption, it perishes for nothing, so it is known that nothing of the debt corresponds to it except at redemption. And if the pledgor authorizes the mortgagee to consume the increments of the pledge by saying, "Whatever increases, consume it," then there is no liability on him, and nothing drops from the pledge because he destroyed it with the pledgor's permission. This is a permission (ibaha), and the absolute permission is allowed to be suspended on a condition and risk, unlike transfer of ownership. If he does not redeem the pledge until it perishes in the mortgagee's hand, the debt is divided over the value of the increment that the mortgagee consumed, and upon him is the value of the original. Whatever corresponds to the original falls, and whatever corresponds to the increment, the mortgagee takes from the pledgor, because the increment perished in the pledgor's property by the mortgagee's action with his authorization, so it is as if the pledgor took and destroyed it, and it is guaranteed against him, so he has the debt. This is mentioned in al-Hidayah and al-Kafi. And in Fatawa Qadikhan and al-Muhit, and attributed to al-Jami': If the value of the mother decreases due to a change in market price and becomes five hundred, or increases and becomes two thousand, while the child remains as it is valued at a thousand, then the debt is divided between them in halves and does not change from what it was. If the mother remains as it is and the value of the child decreases due to a defect or a change in market price and becomes five hundred, then the debt is divided between them into thirds: two-thirds in the mother and one-third in the child. If the value of the child increases to become two thousand, then two-thirds of the debt is in the child and one-third in the mother, so that if the mother perishes, the child remains with two-thirds of the debt. If the mother gives birth to a child and their values are equal, then the mother becomes one-eyed after birth or before, one-fourth of the debt goes, which is two hundred and fifty, because the debt is divided between them in halves, so half of what was in her of the debt goes. And in al-Muntaqa: He pawned land and palm trees for a debt, the value of each being five hundred. The palm trees burned, and other palm trees grew in the land worth five hundred. He said: Half of the debt goes by the burning of the palm trees, and what grew is an increase in the land... like a man who pawned two slave girls, then one of them died, then the remaining one gave birth to a slave girl worth a thousand, then a female slave [worth] a hundred killed her and she was given in compensation, then she gave birth to a child worth a thousand. The debt is divided between them in halves, because the first slave girl remains as she was, and the increase in the pledge has the same ruling as the original, detained and guaranteed like the original, because it is attached to the original contract and becomes as if present in the contract, as in the increments of a sold item. The debt is divided according to the value of the original on the day of receipt and the value of the increase on the day it was received. If the value of the original and the value of the increase on the day it was received were five hundred, the debt is divided between them into thirds, because liability is only obligated by receipt, so the value of each of them on the day of receipt is considered. If the pledge decreases [in value] in his hand, then he adds another pledge, what remains of the debt is divided over the value of the remaining and the value of the increase on the day it was received. Example: If he pawned a slave worth a thousand for a thousand, then he became one-eyed, then he added another pledge, what remains of the debt is divided over the value of the remaining, which is the one-eyed slave, and the value of the added slave into thirds: one-third against the old slave and two-thirds against the added slave, contrary to if she gave birth:
Source pages p. 516

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq (The Full Moon) is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq by Imam al-Nasafi. It discusses the rulings regarding the offspring (inma') or increments produced by a pawned item (rahn). The passage begins with the fundamental rule: the offspring of a pawn, such as a child, dates, milk, and wool, belong to the pledgor (rahin) because they are generated from his property. However, these increments are also part of the pawn itself, meaning they are pledged along with the original asset. If the increment perishes on its own, the pledgor bears the loss without any compensation from the mortgagee (murtahin). If the original pawn perishes but the increment remains, the increment can be redeemed by paying a proportional share of the debt. The debt is divided based on the value of the original and the increment at the time of receipt (qabd). The passage provides a detailed example involving the skin of a sheep: the skin, after the meat is consumed, becomes a pawn for the remaining debt, and it is guaranteed for its value. The discussion then moves to a special case: if the skin is tanned with a substance of value, the mortgagee gains a right to detain the skin for the additional value created by the tanning, similar to the ruling on usurpation (ghasb). This raises a question: does the new right invalidate the original pledge? Two views are presented: one that the original pledge becomes void regarding the skin, making it a new pledge for the tanning value, and another that the original pledge remains but the skin is detained for the tanning value. The text then narrates a report from al-Muntaqa via Hisham ibn Muhammad: if two strangers pawn the same debtor's items without his order, the first becomes a pledge for the entire debt while the second is only pledge for half, due to the principle that the pledge is a surety for the debt, and the second pledge is shared with the first debt. Another report from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad quotes Abu Hanifa on a runaway slave: if the pawned slave runs away and is found, the debt is reduced proportionally because the slave's value has decreased. The commentary then unpacks the matn phrase by phrase. It explains why the offspring is a dependent (tabi') of the original pledge, using analogies and distinctions with other cases like the child of a leased female slave, a guarantor, a usurped item, or a bequeathed usufruct. The dependency means the offspring does not have an independent share in the redemption unless it becomes an intended object (maqsud) when the original is lost. The commentary also addresses the scenario where the pledgor authorizes the mortgagee to consume the increments: the mortgagee is not liable, and the debt is not reduced. If the pledge perishes after consumption, the debt is divided, and the mortgagee takes the value of the consumed increment from the pledgor. Later sections discuss changes in value due to market fluctuations or defects. For example, if the mother's value changes but the child remains, the debt division adjusts proportionally. Detailed calculations are given for various scenarios, emphasizing that the division is based on values at the time of receipt. The passage concludes with an example from al-Muntaqa about pawned land and palms, and another about two female slaves, illustrating how increases are treated as part of the pledge. The overall lesson is that the offspring and other increments of a pawn are governed by the same ruling as the original, but with specific rules for redemption, loss, and division of debt.

Key Terms
دبغ (dabgh): Tanning: processing animal skin to preserve it. In this context, tanning with a valuable substance adds value.
الرهن الأول (al-rahn al-awwal): The original pledge that was established before the tanning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the two views presented by al-Hinduwani, which of the following is a possible consequence of tanning with valuable substance?
A) The skin is no longer part of any pledge.
B) The original pledge remains and the skin is detained for the tanning value.
C) The mortgagee forfeits his right to detain.
D) The tanning is considered a gift to the mortgagee.

Key Takeaway
When a valuable addition is made to a pawn, Hanafi scholars disagree whether it creates a new pledge or extends the original; both views are valid in the school.

advanced
12 min
Apportioning Debt Among Pawned Increments
Explains the division of debt among the pawn and its increments with changing values and permission to consume.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules for dividing a debt among a pawned item and its increments when values change, and explain the ruling when the pledgor authorizes the mortgagee to consume increments.

Core Idea
The debt is apportioned between the original pawn and its increments based on their values at the time of receipt.

The previous lessons established that increments are part of the pledge and redeemed proportionally. But what happens when values change over time? This lesson dives into detailed scenarios: changes in market prices, defects, and explicit permission to consume increments. The commentary provides formulas for reapportioning the debt.

Guided Path
1
Understand the basis of apportionment
The debt is divided according to the value of the original and the increment at the time of receipt (qabd). This is because liability (daman) is established at receipt.
The text says 'يقسم الدين على قيمة الأصل يوم القبض، وعلى قيمة الزيادة يوم قبضت'.
2
Calculate when values change
If the original's value changes (due to market or defect), the division adjusts proportionally. The text gives examples of halves and thirds.
Example: if both are equal, debt divided in half; if one decreases, debt shares adjust.
3
Authorization to consume increments
If the pledgor authorizes the mortgagee to consume the increments (e.g., milk, fruit), the mortgagee is not liable and the debt is not reduced.
This is ibaha (permission), not a transfer of ownership.
4
Apply to scenarios with multiple increments
The final examples show how to handle complex situations like fire destroying part of the pawn, or new growth on land.
New increments (e.g., new palm trees) are treated like new pledges.

آخر وهو كتاب الرهن باب التصرف في الرهن والجناية عليه وجنايته على غيره بدرهم وإنماء الرهن كالولد والتمر واللبن والصوف للراهن وهو رهن مع الأصل ويهلك مجاناً وإن هلك الأصل وبقي النماء فك بحصته ويقسم الدين على قيمته يوم لأنه لم يزل التوى عن اللحم وكان الباقي من الدين ستة فصار الجلد مرهوناً بستة مضموناً بدرهم لأن كل جزء من أجزاء الشاة مرهون بجميع الدين مضمون بمقدار قيمته فكذا الجلد. هذا إذا دبغ بشيء لا قيمة له، فإن دبغ بشيء له قيمة فإنه يستحق المرتهن الحبس بما زاد الدباغ فيه كالغصب، فإذا استحق الحبس بدين آخر حادث هل يبطل الرهن الأول؟ قال الفقيه أبو جعفر الهندواني رحمه الله تعالى : لقائل أن يقول يبطل الرهن الأول في حق الجلد ويصير الجلد رهناً بما زاد الدباغ فيه كما لو رهن الراهن هذه العين بدين حادث، ولقائل أن يقول يبقى الرهن الأول ويصير محبوساً بقيمة الدباغ حتى لا يكون للراهن أن يفتكه ما لم يرد ما بإزائه من الدين وقيمة الدباغ قال في المنتقى : روى هشام عن محمد: رهن أجنبي بدين ألف عبداً بغير أمر المطلوب ثم أجنبي آخر رهنه عبداً آخر بغير أمر المطلوب فهو جائز والأول رهن بألف والثاني رهن بخمسمائة لأن الأول تبع بالرهن ولا رهن بالدين فيكون رهناً بجميع الدين، والثاني رهن وبالدين رهن فلا يصير رهناً إلا بخمسمائة . وذكر الحسن عن أبي حنيفة : إذا أبق العبد الرهن ثم وجد بطل من الدين بقدر نقصان الآبق لأنه بالاباق صار معيباً فإنه لا يشتري بعد الإباق بمثل ما يشتري قبله قال رحمه الله : (وإنماء الرهن كالولد والتمر واللبن والصوف للراهن لأنه متولد من ملكه. قال رحمه الله: (وهو رهن مع الأصل) وهو تبع له والرهن حق متأكد لازم يسري إلى الولد ألا ترى أن الراهن لا يملك به إبطاله بخلاف ولد الجارية حيث لا يسري حكم الجناية إلى الولد ولا يتبع لأنه فيها غير متأكد حتى ينفرد المالك بإبطاله بالفداء بخلاف ولد المستأجرة والكفيلة والمغصوبة وولد الموصي بخدمتها لأن المستأجر حقه في المنفعة دون العين وفي الكفالة الحق يثبت في الذمة والولد لا يتولد من الذمة وفي الغصب إثبات اليد العادية بإزالة اليد المحقة وهو معدوم في الولد ولا يمكن إثباته فيه تبعاً لأنه فعل حسي والتبعية لا تجري في الأوصاف الشرعية، وفي الجارية الموصى بخدمتها المستحق له الخدمة وهي منفعة الأم والولد غير صالح لها قبل الانفصال فلا يكون تبعاً، وبعده لا ينقلب موجباً أيضاً بعد أن انعقد غير موجب . قال رحمه الله : ( ويهلك مجاناً) أي إذا هلك النماء يهلك مجاناً بغير شيء لأن الاتباع لا قسط لها مما يتقابل بالأصل لأنها لم تدخل تحت العقد مقصوداً. قال رحمه الله : (وإن هلك الأصل وبقي النماء فك بحصته) يعني إذا هلك الأصل وهو الرهن وبقي النماء وهو الولد يفتك الولد بحصته من الدين لأنه صار مقصوداً بالفكاك والنماء إذا صار مقصوداً بالفكاك يكون له قسط كولد المبيع لا حصة له من الثمن، ثم إذا صار مقصوداً بالقبض صار له حصة حتى لو هلكت الأم قبل القبض وبقي الولد كان للمشتري أن يأخذه بحصته من الثمن، ولو هلك قبل القبض أمه فيه الفكاك وقيمة الأصل يوم القبض وسقط من الدين حصة الأصل وفك النماء بحصته لا يسقط شيء من الثمن . قال رحمه الله : (ويقسم الدين على قيمته . الفكاك وقيمة الأصل يوم القبض وسقط من الدين حصة الأصل وفك النماء بحصته لأن الولد صار له حصة بالفكاك يوم والأم دخلت في الضمان وقت القبض فيعتبر قيمة كل واحد منهما في وقت اعتباره، ولهذا من لو هلك الولد بعد هلاك أمه قبل الفكاك هلك بغير شيء فيعلم بذلك أنه لا يقابله شيء من الدين إلا عند الفكاك . ولو أذن الراهن للمرتهن في أكل زوائد الرهن بأن قال مهما زاد فكله فلا ضمان عليه ولا يسقط شيء من الرهن لأنه أتلفه بإذن الراهن وهذه إباحة والإطلاق يجوز تعليقه بالشرط والخطر بخلاف التمليك، وإن لم يفتك الرهن حتى هلك في يد المرتهن قسم الدين على قيمة الزيادة التي أكلها المرتهن وعليه قيمة الأصل فما أصاب الأصل سقط، وما أصاب الزيادة أخذه المرتهن من الراهن لأن الزيادة تلفت على ملك الراهن بفعل المرتهن بتسليط منه فصار كأن الراهن أخذه وأتلفه ويكون مضموناً عليه فكان له الدين؛ هكذا ذكره في الهداية والكافي. وفي فتاوى قاضيخان والمحيط وعزاه إلى الجامع : ولو نقصت قيمة الأم بتغير السعر فصارت تساوي خمسمائة أو زادت فصارت تساوي ألفين والولد على حاله يساوي ألفاً فالدين بينهما نصفان ولا يتغير عما كان، وإن كانت الأم على حالها وانتقصت قيمة الولد بعيب . أو بتغير السعر فصارت خمسمائة فالدين بينهما أثلاثاً ثلثان في الأم والثلث في الولد، ولو زادت قيمة الولد فصار يساوي ألفين فثلثا الدين في الولد والثلث في الأم حتى لو هلكت الأم بقي الولد بثلثي الدين. ولو ولدت الأم ولداً وقيمتهما سواء ثم اعورت الأم بعد الولادة أو قبلها ذهب من الدين ربعه وهو مائتان وخمسون لأن الدين ينقسم عليهما نصفين فيذهب نصف ما كان فيها من الدين وفي المنتقى رهن أرضاً ونخلاً بدين قيمة كل واحد خمسمائة فاحترق النخل ونبت في الأرض نخل آخر يساوي خمسمائة قال : يذهب من الدين نصفه باحتراق النخل وما نبت فهو زيادة في الأرض بمنزلة رجل رهن أمتين فماتت إحداهما ثم ولدت الباقية جارية بألف فقتلتها أمة تساوي مائة فدفعت بها ثم ولدت ولداً يساوي ألفاً فالدين بينهما نصفان لأن الأمة الأولى على حالها والزيادة في الرهن حكمها حكم الأصل محبوسة مضمونة كالأصل لأنها تلحق بأصل العقد وصارت كالموجودة في العقد كما في زوائد المبيع. ويقسم الدين على قيمة الأصل يوم القبض، وعلى قيمة الزيادة يوم قبضت، فإن كانت قيمة الأصل وقيمة الزيادة يوم قبضت خمسمائة انقسم الدين عليهما أثلاثاً لأن الضمان إنما يجب بالقبض فتعتبر قيمة كل واحد منهما يوم القبض، فإن نقص الرهن في يده ثم زاد آخر قسم ما بقي من الدين على قيمة الباقي وقيمة الزيادة يوم قبضت مثاله : إذا رهن عبداً يساوي ألفاً بألف فاعور ثم زاده رهناً آخر قسم ما بقي من الدين على قيمة الباقي وهو العبد الأعور وعلى قيمة العبد الزائد أثلاثاً، ثلثه بإزاء العبد القديم وثلثاه بإزاء العبد الزائد بخلاف ما إذا ولدت :
The end and it is the Book of Pledge, Chapter of Disposition in the Pledge and Injury upon it and its Injury upon others. With a dirham. And the growth of the pledge like the child, dates, milk, and wool belongs to the pledgor, and it is a pledge with the original, and it perishes gratuitously. And if the original perishes and the growth remains, it is redeemed by its share, and the debt is divided according to its value on the day... because the [؟] did not cease from the meat, and the remainder of the debt was six, so the skin became pawned for six, guaranteed for a dirham, because every part of the sheep is pawned for the entire debt, guaranteed to the measure of its value, so likewise the skin. This is if it is tanned with something of no value. But if it is tanned with something of value, then the mortgagee is entitled to detainment for the increase of the tanning, like usurpation. So if detainment is due for another new debt, does the first pledge become void? The jurist Abu Ja'far al-Hinduwani, may Allah have mercy on him, said: One might say that the first pledge becomes void regarding the skin and the skin becomes a pledge for the increase of the tanning, as if the pledgor pawned this object for a new debt. And one might say that the first pledge remains and it becomes detained for the value of the tanning, so that the pledgor cannot redeem it unless he pays what is against it of the debt and the value of the tanning. He said in al-Muntaqa: Hisham narrated from Muhammad: A stranger pawned a slave for a debt of a thousand without the order of the debtor, then another stranger pawned another slave without the order of the debtor. It is permissible. The first is a pledge for a thousand, and the second is a pledge for five hundred, because the first is a pledge and there is no debt in the pledge, so it becomes a pledge for the entire debt. The second is a pledge and the debt is a pledge, so it does not become a pledge except for five hundred. And al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa: If the pawned slave runs away and then is found, the debt is remitted by the amount of the deficiency of the runaway, because by running away it became defective, for it is not bought after running away for what it was bought before. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And the growth of the pledge like the child, dates, milk, and wool belongs to the pledgor) because it is generated from his property. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And it is a pledge with the original) and it is a dependent of it. A pledge is an established, binding right that extends to the child. Do you not see that the pledgor cannot invalidate it, unlike the child of the female slave, where the ruling of injury does not extend to the child, nor does it follow, because in it [the pledge] it is not established, such that the owner can invalidate it by ransom, unlike the child of the leased female slave, the guarantor, the usurped, and the one whose service is bequeathed, because the lessee's right is in the usufruct, not the substance; in guarantee, the right is established in the liability, and the child is not generated from the liability; in usurpation, it is establishing a tortious hand by removing a rightful hand, and that is absent in the child and cannot be established in it as a dependent because it is a physical act, and dependency does not run in legal descriptions; and in the female slave whose service is bequeathed, the one entitled to service has a right to the usufruct of the mother, and the child is not suitable for it before separation, so it is not a dependent, and after it, it does not become a cause either after it was not a cause. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And it perishes gratuitously) i.e., if the growth perishes, it perishes gratuitously for nothing, because dependency has no share in what is exchanged with the original, because it did not enter the contract as an intended object. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And if the original perishes and the growth remains, it is redeemed by its share) meaning if the original, which is the pledge, perishes and the growth, which is the child, remains, the child is redeemed by its share of the debt, because it has become an intended object of redemption. When the growth becomes an intended object of redemption, it has a share, like the child of a sold item has no share of the price; but when it becomes an intended object of receipt, it gets a share. So if the mother perishes before receipt and the child remains, the buyer may take it by its share of the price. And if it perishes before receipt, the mother [is] in it. The redemption and the value of the original on the day of receipt, and the share of the original falls from the debt, and the growth is redeemed by its share. Nothing of the price falls. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And the debt is divided according to its value.) The redemption and the value of the original on the day of receipt, and the share of the original falls from the debt, and the growth is redeemed by its share, because the child got a share by redemption on the day the mother entered into liability at the time of receipt, so the value of each of them at the time of its consideration is considered. For this reason, if the child perishes after the mother's death but before redemption, it perishes for nothing, so it is known that nothing of the debt corresponds to it except at redemption. And if the pledgor authorizes the mortgagee to consume the increments of the pledge by saying, "Whatever increases, consume it," then there is no liability on him, and nothing drops from the pledge because he destroyed it with the pledgor's permission. This is a permission (ibaha), and the absolute permission is allowed to be suspended on a condition and risk, unlike transfer of ownership. If he does not redeem the pledge until it perishes in the mortgagee's hand, the debt is divided over the value of the increment that the mortgagee consumed, and upon him is the value of the original. Whatever corresponds to the original falls, and whatever corresponds to the increment, the mortgagee takes from the pledgor, because the increment perished in the pledgor's property by the mortgagee's action with his authorization, so it is as if the pledgor took and destroyed it, and it is guaranteed against him, so he has the debt. This is mentioned in al-Hidayah and al-Kafi. And in Fatawa Qadikhan and al-Muhit, and attributed to al-Jami': If the value of the mother decreases due to a change in market price and becomes five hundred, or increases and becomes two thousand, while the child remains as it is valued at a thousand, then the debt is divided between them in halves and does not change from what it was. If the mother remains as it is and the value of the child decreases due to a defect or a change in market price and becomes five hundred, then the debt is divided between them into thirds: two-thirds in the mother and one-third in the child. If the value of the child increases to become two thousand, then two-thirds of the debt is in the child and one-third in the mother, so that if the mother perishes, the child remains with two-thirds of the debt. If the mother gives birth to a child and their values are equal, then the mother becomes one-eyed after birth or before, one-fourth of the debt goes, which is two hundred and fifty, because the debt is divided between them in halves, so half of what was in her of the debt goes. And in al-Muntaqa: He pawned land and palm trees for a debt, the value of each being five hundred. The palm trees burned, and other palm trees grew in the land worth five hundred. He said: Half of the debt goes by the burning of the palm trees, and what grew is an increase in the land... like a man who pawned two slave girls, then one of them died, then the remaining one gave birth to a slave girl worth a thousand, then a female slave [worth] a hundred killed her and she was given in compensation, then she gave birth to a child worth a thousand. The debt is divided between them in halves, because the first slave girl remains as she was, and the increase in the pledge has the same ruling as the original, detained and guaranteed like the original, because it is attached to the original contract and becomes as if present in the contract, as in the increments of a sold item. The debt is divided according to the value of the original on the day of receipt and the value of the increase on the day it was received. If the value of the original and the value of the increase on the day it was received were five hundred, the debt is divided between them into thirds, because liability is only obligated by receipt, so the value of each of them on the day of receipt is considered. If the pledge decreases [in value] in his hand, then he adds another pledge, what remains of the debt is divided over the value of the remaining and the value of the increase on the day it was received. Example: If he pawned a slave worth a thousand for a thousand, then he became one-eyed, then he added another pledge, what remains of the debt is divided over the value of the remaining, which is the one-eyed slave, and the value of the added slave into thirds: one-third against the old slave and two-thirds against the added slave, contrary to if she gave birth:
Source pages p. 516

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq (The Full Moon) is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq by Imam al-Nasafi. It discusses the rulings regarding the offspring (inma') or increments produced by a pawned item (rahn). The passage begins with the fundamental rule: the offspring of a pawn, such as a child, dates, milk, and wool, belong to the pledgor (rahin) because they are generated from his property. However, these increments are also part of the pawn itself, meaning they are pledged along with the original asset. If the increment perishes on its own, the pledgor bears the loss without any compensation from the mortgagee (murtahin). If the original pawn perishes but the increment remains, the increment can be redeemed by paying a proportional share of the debt. The debt is divided based on the value of the original and the increment at the time of receipt (qabd). The passage provides a detailed example involving the skin of a sheep: the skin, after the meat is consumed, becomes a pawn for the remaining debt, and it is guaranteed for its value. The discussion then moves to a special case: if the skin is tanned with a substance of value, the mortgagee gains a right to detain the skin for the additional value created by the tanning, similar to the ruling on usurpation (ghasb). This raises a question: does the new right invalidate the original pledge? Two views are presented: one that the original pledge becomes void regarding the skin, making it a new pledge for the tanning value, and another that the original pledge remains but the skin is detained for the tanning value. The text then narrates a report from al-Muntaqa via Hisham ibn Muhammad: if two strangers pawn the same debtor's items without his order, the first becomes a pledge for the entire debt while the second is only pledge for half, due to the principle that the pledge is a surety for the debt, and the second pledge is shared with the first debt. Another report from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad quotes Abu Hanifa on a runaway slave: if the pawned slave runs away and is found, the debt is reduced proportionally because the slave's value has decreased. The commentary then unpacks the matn phrase by phrase. It explains why the offspring is a dependent (tabi') of the original pledge, using analogies and distinctions with other cases like the child of a leased female slave, a guarantor, a usurped item, or a bequeathed usufruct. The dependency means the offspring does not have an independent share in the redemption unless it becomes an intended object (maqsud) when the original is lost. The commentary also addresses the scenario where the pledgor authorizes the mortgagee to consume the increments: the mortgagee is not liable, and the debt is not reduced. If the pledge perishes after consumption, the debt is divided, and the mortgagee takes the value of the consumed increment from the pledgor. Later sections discuss changes in value due to market fluctuations or defects. For example, if the mother's value changes but the child remains, the debt division adjusts proportionally. Detailed calculations are given for various scenarios, emphasizing that the division is based on values at the time of receipt. The passage concludes with an example from al-Muntaqa about pawned land and palms, and another about two female slaves, illustrating how increases are treated as part of the pledge. The overall lesson is that the offspring and other increments of a pawn are governed by the same ruling as the original, but with specific rules for redemption, loss, and division of debt.

Key Terms
إباحة (ibaha): Permission; a legal category allowing an action without liability. In the context, the mortgagee's consumption of increments is ibaha, not a transfer of ownership.
يوم القبض (yawm al-qabd): The day of receipt; the date when the mortgagee takes possession of the pledge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the pledgor authorizes the mortgagee to consume the increments of the pawn, what is the effect on the debt?
A) The debt is reduced by the value of increments consumed.
B) The mortgagee is liable for the value of increments.
C) The debt remains unchanged and the mortgagee is not liable.
D) The pledge is considered redeemed for the increments' value.

Key Takeaway
The debt is apportioned proportionally based on receipt values; authorization to consume increments does not reduce the debt or create liability.

Treating Offspring of a Defective Pledge as Pre-Existing for Debt Distribution
Hanafi principle of treating offspring as pre-existing for debt distribution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that offspring of a defective pledge is treated as pre-existing for debt distribution and calculate the shares when an additional pledge is also involved.

Core Idea
Offspring born after a defect is treated as existing before the defect to ensure fair debt coverage.

In the Hanafi school, when a pledged item becomes defective and later produces offspring, the offspring is legally considered to have existed before the defect for the purpose of distributing the debt. This rule, based on istihsan, ensures that the creditor's rights are not unfairly reduced. The present passage from al-Mabsut illustrates this through a detailed calculation involving an added pledge and the death of one pledge. We will unpack the principle and work through the arithmetic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal principle
State the rule: offspring born after a defect is treated as if it existed before the defect, so that some of the fallen debt returns.
This is a specific legal construction (hukm wad'i) for distribution.
2
Recognize the qiyas structure
Identify the asl (pledge existing before defect) and the far' (offspring born after defect). The illa is the need for equitable distribution, making the offspring antedated.
The qiyas is khafi (hidden analogy) based on istihsan.
3
Analyze the example components
Break down the numbers: original slave-girl value 1000, debt 1000; defect halves value (loss 250); added slave-girl worth 500; offspring worth 1000; added slave-girl dies.
The debt after defect is 500? The text is ambiguous; we follow the principle.
4
Apply the antedating rule
Treat the offspring as if it existed before the defect, so it shares in the debt coverage with the mother. The total value to cover the debt is the combined values of mother and offspring (500+1000=1500) plus the added slave-girl (500) but she died, reducing the pool? Actually, the added died, so only mother+offspring remain. The distribution is based on the original shares before death? The text gives fractions: 39/80 for mother+offspring, 21/80 for added.
The calculation uses proportionality: mother+offspring get 39/80 of the debt, added gets 21/80.
5
Calculate the final distribution
Verify: mother+offspring value 1500, added value 500, total 2000. But added dies, so only mother+offspring survive. The debt is 500? The text says 'debt remained with five hundred'. So mother+offspring cover 500 * 39/80 = 243.75? The fractions must be derived differently. The principle ensures equity.
The exact arithmetic requires careful reconstruction; the key is the principle of antedating.

Source Text

وفي المبسوط : أصله أن الولد الحادث والمرهونة بعد العور يجعلان كالموجود قبل العور حتى يعود بسببه بعض ما كان ساقطاً من الدين ومسائله على أنواع : أحدها في الزيادة بعد العور والثاني في الزيادة بعد قضاء بعض المال. الأول : رهن جارية تساوي ألفاً بألف فاعورت فزاد الراهن جارية تساوي خمسمائة فولدت الجارية العوراء ولداً يساوي أ ألفاً ثم ماتت الجارية الزائدة يفتك الجارية العوراء وولدها بتسعة وثلاثين جزءاً من ثمانين جزءاً ونذهب الجارية الزائدة بأحد وعشرين من ثمانين لأنه جعل هذا الولد الحادث بعد الاعورار كالحادث قبل الاعورار فانقسم جميع عليهما ،نصفين فلما اعورت سقط بالاعورار نصف ما فيها وذلك مائتان وخمسون وبقي الدين بخمسمائة، مع[؟]
In al-Mabsut: The principle is that the newborn offspring and the pledged item after a defect are treated as if existing before the defect, so that by it some of what had fallen from the debt returns. Its issues are of types: first, regarding the increase after the defect; second, regarding the increase after payment of part of the property. The first: He pawned a slave-girl worth a thousand for a thousand, then she became defective, then the pawner added another slave-girl worth five hundred, then the defective slave-girl gave birth to a child worth a thousand, then the added slave-girl died. The defective slave-girl and her child are redeemed with thirty-nine eightieths, and the added slave-girl goes with twenty-one eightieths, because this newborn after the defect is made like the one existing before the defect. So the total was divided between them in halves. When she became defective, half of what was in her fell due to the defect, which is two hundred and fifty, and the debt remained with five hundred, with[?]
Source pages p. 520

Commentary
This passage from al-Mabsut states the legal principle that an offspring born after a defect in the pledged item is treated as if it existed before the defect for the purpose of distributing the debt among the pledges. The author provides a detailed calculation example: a slave-girl worth 1000 is pledged for a debt of 1000. She becomes defective (reducing her value by half), then the pawner adds another slave-girl worth 500. The defective slave-girl gives birth to a child worth 1000. Then the added slave-girl dies. The problem is to determine how much of the remaining debt is covered by each surviving pledge. The solution involves dividing the debt proportionally based on values at the time of the contract and treating the offspring as pre-existing. The calculation yields that the defective slave-girl and her child cover 39/80 of the debt, and the added slave-girl covers 21/80. The reasoning is that the offspring is considered as if it existed before the defect, so it shares in the debt coverage. This is a form of istihsan (juristic preference) based on the need to preserve the purpose of the pledge.

Key Terms
الولد الحادث (al-walad al-hadith): The offspring born to the pledged slave-girl after the contract or after a defect occurred.
العور (al-'awar): A defect that reduces the value of the pledged item, here specifically a blemish causing depreciation.

D) 5/8

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi rahn law, offspring born after a defect are legally antedated to before the defect for equitable debt distribution.

Increase in Pledge Valid, Increase in Debt Invalid
Expansion on the matn ruling with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between increasing the pledge (valid) and increasing the debt (invalid) according to the Hanafi school, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute with Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Increasing the pledge is valid by istihsan; increasing the debt using the same pledge is invalid for the majority.

This lesson unpacks the well-known Hanafi ruling that a pawner may add an additional item to an existing pledge, but may not increase the debt secured by that pledge without a new contract. The passage explains the rationale behind this ruling and introduces the position of Abu Yusuf, who disagrees with the majority. We will trace the legal reasoning (ta'lil) and see how the ruling applies in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
The matn states two rulings: increase in the pledge is valid; increase in the debt is not. Note that 'increase in the debt' means making the same pledge secure a new, additional debt, not merely taking another loan.
The new loan itself is valid; the issue is whether the existing pledge covers it.
2
Recognize the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad hold that increasing the debt is invalid. Imam Abu Yusuf holds it is valid. Understand the reasoning behind each position.
Zufar also rejects increase in pledge, but the majority accepts it by istihsan.
3
Analyze the rationale for the majority view
The majority argue that if the increase in debt were valid, it would change the subject of the contract: the pledge would become subordinate to the new debt, reversing the original relationship. This constitutes a prohibited alteration of the contract.
The contracted remains void (bāṭil) if such a change is attempted.
4
Analyze Abu Yusuf's rationale
Abu Yusuf argues that the new debt is a separate disposition; the creditor has authority over the pledge (due to possession) and can make it secure both debts. This is a valid exercise of authority.
He views the pledge as a single asset that can back multiple debts.
5
Determine the muftā bihī and practical difference
The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: increase in debt is invalid. The practical difference (thamarah al-khilāf) appears when a new pledge is added: the majority split the debt proportionally, while Abu Yusuf treats the entire pledge as security for both debts.
Al-Marghinānī in al-Hidāyah confirms the majority view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وتصح الزيادة في الرهن لا في الدين) يعني لو زاد على الرهن رهناً آخر جاز استحساناً خلافاً لزفر، والزيادة في الدين لا تصح عندهما. وقال أبو بوسف رحمه الله تعالى : تجوز الزيادة في الدين أيضاً، ويجوز أن يكون للمرتهن على الراهن دين آخر فيجعل الرهن رهناً بهما. ولأبي يوسف رحمه الله تعالى أن هذه الزيادة تصير بعض الرهن رهناً بالزيادة وهو دين حادث مع بقاء القبض في الأصل وهذا تصرف في الرهن لا في الدين ولهما ولاية التصرف فيكون مشروعاً تصحيحاً لتصرفهما. ولهما أن الراهن تصرف في الرهن لا في الدين ولو صحت الزيادة في الدين تصير زيادة في الرهن تبعاً فينقلب المتبوع تابعاً وفيه تغيير المشروع وتبديل الموضوع وهو العقد باطل. وفي العناية : ولو قال زدتك هذا العبد مع الأم قسم الدين على قيمة الأم يوم وعلى قيمة الزيادة يوم القبض فما أصاب الأم قسم عليها وعلى ولدها لأن الزيادة دخلت الأم، فإن ماتت الأم بعد الزيادة ذهب ما كان فيها وبقي الولد والزيادة بما فيها فلا يبطل الحكم بالزيادة، ولو مات الولد بعد الزيادة ذهب بغير شيء. وفي العناية أيضاً : ولو قال زدتك هذا رهناً مع الولد جاز العقد ويكون رهناً مع الولد دون الأم فينظر إلى قيمة الولد يوم الفكاك وإلى قيمة الأم يوم العقد، فما أصاب الولد قسم على قيمته يوم الفكاك وقيمة العبد قبضه لأنه دخل في ضمانه بالقبض، فإن مات بعد الزيادة بطلت لأنه إذا هلك خرج من يوم العقد وصار كأن لم يكن فيبطل الحكم في الزيادة. والمراد بقوله أن الزيادة في الدين لا تصح أن رهناً لا يكون رهناً بالزيادة وأما نفس زيادة الدين على الدين فصحيحة لأن الاستدانة بعد الاستدانة قبل قضاء الدين الأول جائز إجماعاً، وإذا صحت الزيادة في الرهن ثم قبضت قسم الدين على قيمتها يوم قبضها وعلى قيمة الأول يوم قبضه وظاهر عبارة إطلاق المؤلف زيادة الدين شرط في مقابلتها رهناً أولاً، والمنقول التفصيل قال في المبسوط : رهنه عبداً قيمته ألف ثم زاده المرتهن بخمسمائة على إن زاده الراهن أمة العبد الرهن بالدين كله فالأمة نصفها رهن مع العبد بخمسمائة عندهما قال أبو يوسف : هما رهن بالألف. رهنه عبداً قيمته بخمسمائة، مع
He (the author) said: (And the increase in the pledge is valid, not in the debt) meaning: if he adds another pledge to the pledge, it is permissible by istihsan, contrary to Zufar. And the increase in the debt is not valid according to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). And Abu Yusuf said: Increase in the debt is also permissible, and it is permissible for the creditor to have another debt against the debtor and make the pledge a pledge for both. For Abu Yusuf, this increase makes part of the pledge a pledge for the increase, which is a new debt while the possession remains on the original, and this is a disposition on the pledge, not on the debt, and they have authority to dispose, so it is legislated to validate their disposition. For them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), the pawner disposed on the pledge, not on the debt. If the increase in the debt were valid, it would become an increase in the pledge as a subordinate, thus the subordinate becomes the subject, and there is a change in the legislated and a substitution of the subject, which makes the contract void. In al-Inayah: If he said 'I add this slave to you with the mother,' the debt is divided on the value of the mother on the day (of contract) and on the value of the increase on the day of possession, so what hits the mother is divided on her and on her child, because the increase enters the mother. If the mother dies after the increase, what was in her goes, and the child and the increase remain with what is in them, so the ruling on the increase does not become void. If the child dies after the increase, it goes for nothing. And in al-Inayah also: If he said 'I add this to you as a pledge with the child,' the contract is valid and it becomes a pledge with the child, not with the mother. Then one looks at the value of the child on the day of redemption and the value of the mother on the day of contract. What hits the child is divided on its value on the day of redemption and the value of the slave at its possession, because it entered into its guarantee by possession. If it dies after the increase, it becomes void because when it perishes, it exits from the day of contract and becomes as if it had not been, so the ruling on the increase is void. What is meant by his saying that the increase in the debt is not valid is that a pledge cannot be a pledge for the increase. As for the increase of debt upon debt itself, it is valid because taking a loan after a loan before repaying the first debt is permissible by consensus. And if the increase in the pledge is valid then it is possessed, the debt is divided on its value on the day of its possession and on the value of the first on the day of its possession. The apparent purport of the author's statement conditions the increase in debt against a pledge first. The transmitted detail: He said in al-Mabsut: He pawned a slave worth one thousand, then the creditor increased (the debt) by five hundred on condition that the pawner add a slave-girl to the slave as a pledge for the entire debt. So the slave-girl is half a pledge with the slave for five hundred according to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad); Abu Yusuf said: They are both a pledge for one thousand. He pawned a slave worth five hundred, with[?]
Source pages p. 521

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the matn statement 'وتصح الزيادة في الرهن لا في الدين' (Increase in the pledge is valid, not in the debt). The commentator explains the ruling and the intra-Hanafi dispute. The main positions: According to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybani), if a pawner adds an additional pledge to the existing pledge, it is valid by istihsan (juristic preference), contrary to Zufar who rejects it. However, if the creditor and debtor agree to increase the debt (i.e., add a new loan) and make the same pledge secure both debts, that is not valid according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf differs, allowing the increase in debt as well, reasoning that the new debt is a separate disposition and the pledge remains in possession, so it can secure both debts. The commentary elaborates with examples from al-Inayah and al-Mabsut, showing how the distribution works when there are multiple pledges and when offspring are involved. A crucial distinction is made: the increase in the debt as a contract (i.e., taking an additional loan) is valid by consensus, but making the same pledge a security for that increase without a new contract of pledge is invalid according to the majority Hanafi view. The passage also discusses scenarios where the pledge is increased with a condition about the mother or child, illustrating the legal consequences. Ultimately, the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that increasing the pledge is valid, but increasing the debt (i.e., making the same pledge cover a new debt without a new pledge contract) is not, unless done with a new pledge.

Key Terms
الزيادة في الرهن (al-ziyadah fi al-rahn): Adding an additional pledged item to an existing pledge contract.
الزيادة في الدين (al-ziyadah fi al-dayn): Increasing the amount of the debt secured by the same pledge without a new pledge contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Valid only if the debtor agrees
D) Invalid, but the new debt itself is void

Key Takeaway
Increasing the debt secured by the same pledge is not valid in the Hanafi school; a new pledge is required for new debt.

Increasing the Pledge vs Increasing the Debt
Intra-Hanafi dispute on pledge modifications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on increasing the debt secured by an existing pledge, explain the proofs of each side, and identify the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Increasing the pledge is valid; increasing the debt is not—unless you are Abu Yusuf.

In pledge (rahn) contracts, parties sometimes want to add more collateral or borrow more money under the same pledge. The Hanafi school has a clear rule: you can add more items to the pledge, but you cannot increase the debt covered by the same pledge without a new contract. However, Imam Abu Yusuf disagreed, arguing that an additional debt can be secured by the same pledge if the parties agree. This lesson unpacks that intra-Hanafi dispute and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two issues
The passage discusses two distinct modifications: (a) increasing the pledge (adding another item as collateral) and (b) increasing the debt (the creditor lends more money under the same pledge). Note the ruling for each.
Increasing the pledge is valid by istihsan; increasing the debt is disputed.
2
State the Sahibayn's position and proof
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the two Sahibayn) hold that increasing the debt is invalid. Their proof: the mortgagor's disposition is in the pledge, not the debt; if the debt increases, the debt becomes the primary object and the pledge follows, inverting the intended relationship.
This is the mufta bihi position.
3
State Abu Yusuf's position and proof
Abu Yusuf holds that increasing the debt is valid. He argues that the additional debt creates a new pledge by attaching to a part of the original pledge, which is a disposition in the pledge—something the parties have authority to do.
He emphasizes retention of possession.
4
Consider Zufar's view
Zufar even disallows increasing the pledge, but the passage notes this is contrary to the relied-upon view (istihsan).
Zufar's view is not accepted in the madhhab.
5
Apply the mufta bihi ruling
The relied-upon position is that of the Sahibayn. In practice, if a debtor wants to borrow more money, he must either settle the first loan and create a new pledge, or add a separate pledge for the new debt.
This avoids confusion over what the pledge secures.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتصح الزيادة في الرهن لا في الدين يعني لو زاد على الرهن رهناً آخر جاز استحساناً خلافاً لزفر، والزيادة في الدين لا تصح عندهما. وقال أبو يوسف رحمه الله تعالى : تجوز الزيادة في الدين أيضاً، ويجوز أن يكون للمرتهن على الراهن دين آخر فيجعل الرهن رهناً بهما. ولأبي يوسف رحمه الله تعالى أن هذه الزيادة تصير بعض الرهن رهناً بالزيادة وهو دين حادث مع بقاء القبض في الأصل وهذا تصرف في الرهن لا في الدين ولهما ولاية التصرف فيكون مشروعاً تصحيحاً لتصرفهما. ولهما أن الراهن تصرف في الرهن لا في الدين ولو صحت الزيادة في الدين تصير زيادة في الرهن تبعاً فينقلب المتبوع تابعاً وفيه تغيير المشروع وتبديل الموضوع وهو العقد باطل.
And the increase in the pledge is valid, not in the debt. That is, if he adds another pledge to the pledge, it is permissible by istihsan, contrary to Zufar. And the increase in the debt is not valid according to them (the two Sahibayn). And Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, said: The increase in the debt is also permissible, and it is permissible for the mortgagee to have another debt against the mortgagor and make the pledge a pledge for both. And for Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, is that this increase makes part of the pledge a pledge for the increase, which is a new debt, with the retention of possession in the original, and this is a disposition in the pledge, not in the debt, and they have authority to dispose, so it is legislated to validate their disposition. And for them (the two Sahibayn), the mortgagor disposed in the pledge, not in the debt, and if the increase in the debt were valid, it would become an increase in the pledge as a follower, and the followed would become a follower, and that involves changing the legislated, and altering the subject, and the contract is void.
Source pages p. 521

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the validity of increasing the pledge versus increasing the debt. The author (Ibn Nujaym) states the ruling from the matn: increasing the pledge is valid, but increasing the debt is not. He then explains that according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the two Sahibayn), if the mortgagor adds another pledge to the existing pledge, it is valid by istihsan, contrary to Zufar who disallows it. However, increasing the debt (i.e., using the same pledge for an additional debt) is not valid in their view. Abu Yusuf disagrees and holds that increasing the debt is also permissible; the pledge can secure both the original debt and the additional debt. Abu Yusuf argues that the additional pledge becomes a pledge for the new debt while the original possession remains, making it a disposition in the pledge, which is within the authority of the parties. The Sahibayn respond that the mortgagor's action is in the pledge, not the debt; if increasing the debt were valid, the debt would become the primary subject and the pledge would follow, which reverses the intended relationship and alters the contract's subject, rendering the contract void.

Key Terms
زيادة في الرهن (ziyada fi al-rahn): Adding another item as additional collateral for the existing debt.
زيادة في الدين (ziyada fi al-dayn): Increasing the amount of the debt secured by the same pledge without a new contract.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; here it justifies the validity of increasing the pledge despite qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on increasing the debt secured by a pledge according to the two Sahibayn?
A) It is valid by istihsan.
B) It is invalid (batil).
C) It is valid only if the debtor adds another pledge.
D) It is valid according to Zufar.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, increasing the pledge is valid by istihsan; increasing the debt secured by the same pledge without a new contract is invalid according to the relied-upon position of the Sahibayn.

Replacing a Pledge with Another
Ruling on the legal status when a mortgagor replaces a pledge with another of equal value.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the legal status of the original and substitute pledges when a mortgagor replaces a pledge with another of equal value, and explain the reasoning based on possession and liability.

Core Idea
Handing over a substitute pledge does not release the original; it remains in liability until formally returned.

When a debtor wishes to replace one pledged asset with another, the legal status of both assets matters. Does the original pledge automatically release? Does the substitute immediately become a full pledge? The Hanafi school provides a clear framework: the original pledge remains in the mortgagee's liability until physically returned, while the substitute is held as a trust. This lesson explains the reasoning and conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the asset
The mortgagor (debtor) originally pledges an asset (first slave) to the mortgagee (creditor). Later, the mortgagor offers a different asset (second slave) of equal value as a substitute.
Both assets are of equal value per the text.
2
Determine the status of the original pledge
The original pledge remains a valid pledge under the mortgagee's liability (daman). It does not exit liability because possession (qabd) and debt continue.
Liability is only removed by returning the asset or discharging the debt.
3
Determine the status of the substitute
The substitute is held as a trust (amanah) by the mortgagee. It is not yet a pledge because the original is still in effect.
The mortgagee is not liable for loss of the substitute without negligence.
4
Identify the condition for transition
Only when the original pledge is physically returned to the mortgagor does the substitute enter the mortgagee's liability and become the actual pledge.
The text explicitly states: 'When the first is returned, the second enters his liability.'
5
Explain the rationale
The first pledge entered liability by possession and debt; it cannot exit until those are removed. Both parties agreed to replace, so the second is held in trust until the first is formally released.
This prevents unilateral release of collateral.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ومن رهن عبد بألف فدفع عبد آخر رهنا مكان الأول وقيمة كل ألف فالأول رهن حتى يرده إلى الراهن والمرتهن من الآخر أمين حتى يجعله مكان الأول لأن الأول دخل في ضمانه بالقبض والدين وهما باقيان فلا يخرج عن إلا برفعهما، وإذا دخل بقي الأول في ضمانه ولا يدخل الثاني في ضمانه لأنهما رضيا بأحدهما، فإذا رد الأول دخل الثاني في ضمانه.
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And whoever pledges a slave for one thousand, then hands over another slave as a pledge in place of the first, and the value of each is one thousand, then the first is a pledge until he returns it to the mortgagor, and the mortgagee is a trustee over the other until he makes it in place of the first because the first entered his liability (daman) by possession and the debt, and both remain, so it does not leave except by removing them. And when it entered, the first remains in his liability, and the second does not enter his liability because they both agreed on one of them. Then when the first is returned, the second enters his liability.
Source pages p. 521

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on replacing a pledge with another of equal value. The author explains that if a person pledges a slave for a debt of 1,000, and later gives another slave of the same value to replace the first, the legal status of the two slaves differs: the first slave remains in the mortgagee's liability (daman) as a full pledge, while the second is held as a trust (amana) in the mortgagee's hands until the first is formally returned to the mortgagor. The reason is that the first slave entered the mortgagee's liability through possession (qabd) and the debt continues, so it cannot exit liability without the debt being discharged or the pledge explicitly released. The second slave does not automatically enter liability because both parties intended to replace the first, so they are satisfied with one of them. Only when the first is returned does the second become the actual pledge.

Key Terms
الرهن الأول (al-rahn al-awwal): The original pledged item that remains in the mortgagee's liability until replaced.
أمين (amin): Trustee; the mortgagee holds the second slave as a trust (amana) until the substitution is complete.
ضمان (daman): Liability; the mortgagee becomes liable for the pledged item upon possession.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) It is not accepted at all.
D) It belongs to the mortgagee.

Key Takeaway
The original pledge remains in the mortgagee's liability until it is physically returned; the substitute is held as a trust until then.

Distribution of Debt When Pledged Items Perish: Proportional Allocation
Explaining distribution of debt when pledges and offspring perish

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the remaining debt and allocate surviving pledges when multiple items are given as security and some perish, applying the Hanafi principle of proportional distribution.

Core Idea
When a pledged item perishes, the debt is reduced proportionally; surviving pledges secure the reduced debt including offspring.

This passage from the Hanafi commentary Al-Bahr al-Raiq presents several scenarios illustrating the legal consequences when multiple pledges (including their offspring) are destroyed while in the mortgagee's possession. The author calculates how the debt is distributed among the remaining assets. Understanding these calculations is crucial for correctly applying the rules of pledge (rahn) in Hanafi fiqh, as the debt does not vanish but attaches to surviving collateral.

Guided Path
1
Identify the debt and initial pledges
Determine the total debt and the values of each pledged item. Note that offspring of pledged slaves are also part of the pledge.
e.g., debt = 1000, first pledge a slave worth X, second pledge a slave-girl worth Y, etc.
2
Account for offspring
Offspring of pledged slaves are considered part of the pledge itself. Their value must be added to the mother's value for distribution purposes.
If a slave-girl gives birth while pledged, the child is also a pledge.
3
Determine which items perish
Specify which pledges (slaves, slave-girls, or their offspring) are destroyed. Their values are deducted from the debt proportionally.
Only the perished items' values affect the reduction.
4
Calculate the remaining debt
The debt is reduced by the value of the perished items. The reduction is proportional: if an item was securing a portion of the debt, that portion is reduced by the item's value.
If a pledge worth 500 secures 500 of a 1000 debt, and it perishes, 500 of debt is extinguished; the remaining 500 is secured by other pledges.
5
Allocate surviving pledges
The remaining debt is secured by the surviving pledges (including offspring). The allocation is based on the relative values of those pledges.
If multiple survive, each secures a proportional share of the remaining debt.

Source Text

Ruling on Substituting a Pledge
Ruling with proof on substitution of a pledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on substituting a pledge and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute over contract renewal.

Core Idea
Substituting a pledge does not release the original; it remains until returned, and the substitute is a trust.

This lesson examines a classic scenario in Hanafi contract law: a mortgagor offers a substitute pledge of equal value while the original is still held. The author of Kanz al-Daqaiq clarifies the legal status of both items and addresses a scholarly dispute over whether a new contract is necessary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal scenario
A debtor pledges a slave for a debt, then later offers a second slave of equal value as a substitute. The question is the status of both pledges.
Value is assumed equal per the text.
2
Determine the ruling on the original pledge
The original remains a valid pledge until physically returned to the pledgor. The debt and possession of the original are unchanged.
The original is not automatically replaced.
3
Determine the status of the substitute
The substitute is held as a trust (amanah) only, not as a pledge with guarantee (daman), until the original is returned.
The mortgagee is not liable for the substitute as a pledge.
4
Analyze the dispute on contract renewal
Some Hanafi scholars require a new contract (tajdid al-aqd) because taking possession of a trust does not count as taking possession of a pledge. Others disagree, arguing the pledgor voluntarily offers the substitute as a trust and possession of a trust can substitute for possession of a trust.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ومن رهن عبد بألف فدفع عبد آخر رهنا مكان الأول وقيمة كل ألف فالأول رهن حتى يرده إلى الراهن والمرتهن من الآخر أمين حتى يجعله مكان الأول لأن الأول دخل في ضمانه بالقبض والدين وهما باقيان فلا يخرج عن إلا برفعهما، وإذا دخل بقي الأول في ضمانه ولا يدخل الثاني في ضمانه لأنهما رضيا بأحدهما، فإذا رد الأول دخل الثاني في ضمانه . ثم قيل : يشترط تجديد العقد فيه لأن قبض الأمانة لا ينوب عن قبض الضمان وقيل : لا يشترط لأن الراهن تبرع وعينه أمانة على ما عرف وقبض الأمانة ينوب عن قبض الأمانة
He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: 'Whoever pledges a slave for a thousand and then submits another slave as a pledge in place of the first, and the value of each is a thousand, then the first is a pledge until he returns it to the pledgor, and the mortgagee from the other is a trustee until he places it in the place of the first. Because the first entered into his guarantee by possession and the debt, and both remain, so it does not leave except by removing them. And when it enters, the first remains in his guarantee, and the second does not enter his guarantee because they both agreed to one of them. So if he returns the first, the second enters his guarantee. Then it is said: a renewal of the contract is required because the taking of a trust does not substitute for the taking of a pledge. And it is said: it is not required because the pledgor gratuitously offered and designated it as a trust according to what is known, and the taking of a trust substitutes for the taking of a trust.'
Source pages p. 522

Commentary
This passage deals with the substitution of a pledge. The author presents the ruling: if a debtor replaces an existing pledge with another of equal value, the original pledge remains in effect until it is returned to the pledgor. The substitute is merely a trust (amanah) in the mortgagee's hands until the original pledge is properly returned. The reasoning is that the original pledge had already entered into the mortgagee's guarantee (daman) through possession (qabd) and the existence of the debt, both of which remain unchanged. The substitute does not acquire the same guarantee until the original is returned. Then two opinions are mentioned regarding whether a new contract (tajdid al-aqd) is needed: some say yes because the possession of an amanah cannot substitute for the possession of a pledge; others say no because the pledgor voluntary offers it and it is designated as a trust, and possession of a trust can substitute for possession of a trust.

Key Terms
ضمان (daman): Guarantee; the liability of the mortgagee for the pledge.
قبض (qabd): Taking possession; the act of taking physical control of the pledge.
تجديد العقد (tajdid al-aqd): Renewal of the contract; whether a new pledge contract is needed when substituting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Only after the original pledge is returned to the mortgagor.

Key Takeaway
The original pledge remains valid until returned; the substitute is a trust until the original is returned, and the need for a new contract is disputed within the Hanafi school.

Destruction of Pledge after Acquittal: Ruling by Istihsan
Ruling on the destruction of a pledge after acquittal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a pledge is destroyed after the creditor acquits the debt, and explain why istihsan overrides strict analogy.

Core Idea
When the debt is released, the pledge loses its collateral status; its destruction incurs no liability by istihsan.

This short passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq presents a ruling that might seem counterintuitive: if a creditor forgives a debt and then the collateral perishes, the creditor is not liable. Understanding the legal reasoning—istihsan over qiyas—is essential for grasping the Hanafi approach to pledges. We'll unpack the ruling, its proof, and the intra-madhhab disagreement with Zufar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the destruction of a pledge after the creditor acquits the debtor of the debt or gifts the debt to him. The ruling is that it is destroyed without compensation (halka bighayri shay).
The ruling is based on istihsan, not strict analogy.
2
Identify the proof (dalil)
The author cites istihsan (juristic preference) as the basis. The strict qiyas would hold the creditor liable because the pledge is a guarantee (amana) in his hand, but istihsan departs from this because the debt is extinguished, so the pledge no longer secures anything.
The dalil is not a text but a principle: the purpose of the pledge is to secure the debt.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Zufar disagrees, holding that the pledge remains guaranteed (madhmun) even after the debt is extinguished, so he would require compensation.
This shows that even within the Hanafi school there are differing opinions.
4
Explain the rationale of istihsan
The pledge exists solely to secure the debt. Once the debt is extinguished by acquittal or gift, the pledge loses its purpose and reverts to being a mere trust (amana) in the creditor's hands, and any loss is borne by the owner (the debtor). This is more equitable, hence istihsan.
The key is the change in the underlying obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو أبرأ المرتهن الراهن عن الدين أو وهبه منه ثم هلك الرهن في يد المرتهن هلك بغير شيء استحساناً خلافاً لزفر وقد مر
And if the mortgagee acquits the pledgor of the debt or gifts it to him, and then the pledge is destroyed in the mortgagee's hand, it is destroyed without compensation, by istihsan, contrary to Zafar (Zufar), and it has passed.
Source pages p. 522

Commentary
This passage addresses the scenario where the creditor (mortgagee) releases the debtor from the debt or gifts the debt to him. If after such a transaction, the pledge perishes while in the mortgagee's possession, it is considered destroyed without any compensation (i.e., the mortgagee is not liable). This ruling is based on istihsan (juristic preference), which is a departure from qiyas. The text notes that this is contrary to the opinion of Zufar (a Hanafi scholar who followed stricter analogy). The phrase 'and it has passed' indicates that this ruling has been mentioned earlier in the work.

Key Terms
إبراء (ibra'): Acquittal; release of the debtor from the debt by the creditor.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; a method of departing from strict analogy in favor of a more equitable ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if the creditor acquits the debt and then the pledge is destroyed, what is the ruling?
A) The creditor must compensate.
B) It is destroyed without compensation (istihsan).
C) It is considered stolen.
D) The debtor is fined.

Key Takeaway
When a debt is extinguished by acquittal or gift, the pledge loses its guarantee, and its destruction is without compensation by istihsan.
