Rulings on Transactions with the Debt and Effect on Pledge
Rulings on when the creditor purchases with the debt or settles, and the pledge is then destroyed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three scenarios where the creditor transacts with the debt and explain the consequence of pledge destruction on each transaction.

Core Idea
If the pledge is destroyed after a new arrangement, the arrangement collapses and the debt stands.

This passage clarifies a critical principle in pledge law: actions that alter the debt arrangement do not sever the pledge. Even if the creditor agrees to a new arrangement, the pledge remains attached to the original debt. If the pledge is destroyed after such an arrangement, the arrangement collapses, and the debt stands.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three actions
List the three actions mentioned: creditor buys with the debt, creditor settles from the debt in exchange for a substance, or debtor transfers the debt via hawala.
Each action involves a shift in the debt arrangement.
2
Recognise the condition
Note that these actions occur while a valid pledge (rahn) secures the debt.
3
Analyse the consequence of destruction
If the pledge is destroyed after the action, the hawala becomes void and is considered destroyed under the debt, and the purchase and settlement become void.
The destruction triggers nullification.
4
Derive the legal principle
The pledge remains tied to the original debt; substitute transactions are conditional on the pledge's existence. Destruction invalidates them.
This preserves the creditor's security interest.
5
Apply to a new scenario
Example: Creditor buys a horse from debtor for the debt, then original pledge is destroyed. The purchase becomes void, debt revives.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا اشترى بالدين عيناً أو صالح من الدين على عين أو حال الراهن المرتهن بالدين على غيره ثم الرهن بطلت الحوالة وهلك بالدين وبطل الشراء والصلح
And if he purchases a substance with the debt, or settles from the debt for a substance, or the pledgor transfers the debt to someone else (hawala), and then the pledge (is destroyed?) the hawala becomes void and it is destroyed under the debt, and the purchase and settlement become void.
Source pages p. 522

Commentary
This passage outlines three scenarios where the creditor takes action regarding the debt—purchasing an item in lieu of the debt, reaching a settlement by transferring a specific asset, or the debtor making a hawala (transfer of debt) to another party. If after any of these transactions, the original pledge is destroyed, the hawala is nullified and the pledge is considered to have perished under the debt (meaning the creditor loses his claim against the substitute asset). Consequently, the purchase and settlement are also invalidated. This preserves the original debt and pledge.

Key Terms
حوالة (hawala): Transfer of debt; a contractual arrangement where the debtor transfers the liability to a third party.
صلح (sulh): Settlement; a contract of compromise to end a dispute.
رهن (rahn): Pledge; a contract where property is given as security for a debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens to a hawala (debt transfer) if the original pledge is destroyed after the transfer?
A) It remains valid.
B) It becomes void.
C) The new debtor must provide a pledge.
D) The pledge is transferred to the new debtor.

Key Takeaway
Any transaction altering the debt arrangement is void if the original pledge is destroyed; the debt stands and the pledge is lost.

Rahn — Pledge
intermediate
8 min
Mutual Acknowledgment of No Debt: Effect on the Pledge Guarantee
Intra-Hanafi dispute on pledge guarantee

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling when both pledgor and pledgee agree there was no debt, and determine whether the pledge remains guaranteed based on the timing of the agreement.

Core Idea
The timing of mutual acknowledgment determines the pledge's guarantee: if after destruction, it remains; if before, it does not.

In a pledge contract, the mortgagee is liable for the pledged item unless the debt is extinguished. But what if both parties later agree that there was never a debt? This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether such mutual acknowledgment (tasāduq) voids the guarantee. The ruling depends on when the acknowledgment occurs relative to the destruction of the pledge.

Guided Path
1
Understand the scenario
Both the pledgor and pledgee mutually affirm that there was no debt. Consider two timings: before the pledge is destroyed, or after.
2
Identify Shams al-A'imma's position
In Al-Mabsut, he holds that if mutual acknowledgment occurs after destruction, the guarantee remains because the debt was apparently valid at the time of destruction. If before, the guarantee does not remain because the debt is negated from the origin.
This view separates liability based on timing.
3
Identify al-Isbijabi's refinement
Al-Isbijabi notes that earlier scholars differed on the case where acknowledgment precedes destruction. He declares the correct view (al-sawab) that the pledge is not destroyed as a guaranteed item; the mortgagee is not liable.
This aligns with the second part of Shams al-A'imma's position.
4
Understand the legal basis
The guarantee is tied to the apparent existence of the debt. Mutual acknowledgment does not retroactively erase the debt's legal effect for the period before the acknowledgment.
Key principle: a debt cannot be extinguished by mere acknowledgment for past events.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, if the pledge is destroyed after acknowledgment, the mortgagee is not liable. If destroyed before, the mortgagee remains liable, and the acknowledgment does not absolve him.
The thamarah al-khilaf is a difference in liability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا تصادقا على أن لا دين ثم هلك يهلك بالدين لتوهم وجوب الدين بالتصادق فتكون الجهة باقية. وفي الكافي ذكر شمس الأئمة في المبسوط : إذا تصادقا على أن لا دين بقي ضمان الرهن إذا كان تصادقهما بعد هلاك الرهن لأن الدين كان واجباً ظاهراً وظهوره يكفي لضمان الرهن، وأما إذا تصادقا قبله يبقى الدين من الأصل وضمان الرهن لا يبقى بدون الرهن. وذكر الاسبيجابي أنهما إذا تصادقا قبل الهلاك ثم هلك الرهن اختلف مشايخنا فيه والصواب أنه لا يهلك مضموناً
And if they mutually agree that there is no debt, and then it perishes, it perishes under the debt due to the illusion of the obligation of the debt by their mutual agreement, so the basis remains. In al-Kafi, Shams al-A'imma mentioned in al-Mabsut: If they mutually agree that there is no debt, the guarantee of the pledge remains if their mutual agreement occurs after the destruction of the pledge, because the debt was apparent and its appearance suffices for the guarantee of the pledge. But if they mutually agree before it, the debt remains from the origin and the guarantee of the pledge does not remain without the pledge. And al-Isbijabi mentioned that if they mutually agree before destruction and then the pledge is destroyed, our scholars differed, and the correct view is that it is not destroyed as a guaranteed item.
Source pages p. 522

Commentary
This passage deals with the scenario where both the pledgor and pledgee (mortgagee) affirm that there was no debt. The ruling depends on the timing. If they agree after the pledge has been destroyed, the guarantee (daman) of the pledge remains because the debt was apparently valid at the time. However, if they agree before destruction, the debt remains from the origin (i.e., the debt is still considered existing) but the guarantee of the pledge does not remain without the pledge. Then al-Isbijabi is quoted saying that the scholars differed and the correct view is that the pledge is not destroyed as a guaranteed item (i.e., the mortgagee is not liable). The passage thus presents an intra-Hanafi disagreement with a preferred opinion.

Key Terms
تصادق (tasāduq): Mutual agreement; both parties affirming a fact, here that there is no debt.
ضمان (daman): Guarantee; the liability of the mortgagee for the pledged item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view in the passage, if the pledgor and pledgee agree there was no debt before the pledge is destroyed, what is the status of the pledge?
A) It is guaranteed.
B) It is not guaranteed.
C) The debt is doubled.
D) The pledge becomes a trust.

Key Takeaway
The timing of mutual acknowledgment of no debt relative to the pledge's destruction determines whether the mortgagee remains liable: after destruction = liable; before = not liable.
